Cotton City Administrative Officer ____________ Paula Martin City Clerk ____________ James Skipper City Attorney PREFACE     This Code constitutes a recodification of the general and permanent ordinances of the City of Americus, Georgia.     Source materials used in the preparation of the Code were the 1986 Code and ordinances adopted by the city council. The source of each section is included in the history note appearing in parentheses at the end thereof. The absence of such a note indicates that the section is new and was adopted for the first time with the adoption of the Code. By use of the comparative tables appearing in the back of this Code, the reader can locate any section of the prior Code, and any ordinance included herein.     The chapters of the Code have been conveniently arranged in alphabetical order, and the various sections within each chapter have been catchlined to facilitate usage. Notes which tie related sections of the Code together and which refer to relevant state law have been included. A table listing the state law citations and setting forth their location within the Code is included at the back of this Code. Chapter and Section Numbering System     The chapter and section numbering system used in this Code is the same system used in many state and local government codes. Each section number consists of two parts separated by a dash. The figure before the dash refers to the chapter number, and the figure after the dash refers to the position of the section within the chapter. Thus, the second section of chapter 1 is numbered 1-2, and the first section of chapter 6 is 6-1. Under this system, each section is identified with its chapter, and at the same time new sections can be inserted in their proper place by using the decimal system for amendments. For example, if new material consisting of one section that would logically come between sections 6-1 and 6-2 is desired to be added, such new section would be numbered 6-1.5. New articles and new divisions may be included in the same way or, in the case of articles, may be placed at the end of the chapter embracing the subject, and, in the case of divisions, may be placed at the end of the article embracing the subject. The next successive number shall be assigned to the new article or division. New chapters may be included by using one of the reserved chapter numbers. Care should be taken that the alphabetical arrangement of chapters is maintained when including new chapters. Page Numbering System     The page numbering system used in this Code is a prefix system. The letters to the left of the colon are an abbreviation which represents a certain portion of the volume. The number to the right of the colon represents the number of the page in that portion. In the case of a chapter of the Code, the number to the left of the colon indicates the number of the chapter. In the case of an appendix to the Code, the letter immediately to the left of the colon indicates the letter of the appendix. The following are typical parts of codes of ordinances, which may or may not appear in this Code at this time, and their corresponding prefixes: CHARTER CHT:1 CHARTER COMPARATIVE TABLE CHTCT:1 CODE CD1:1 CODE APPENDIX CDA:1 CODE COMPARATIVE TABLES CCT:1 STATE LAW REFERENCE TABLE SLT:1 CHARTER INDEX CHTi:1 CODE INDEX CDi:1  Indexes     The indexes have been prepared with the greatest of care. Each particular item has been placed under several headings, some of which are couched in lay phraseology, others in legal terminology, and still others in language generally used by local government officials and employees. There are numerous cross references within the indexes themselves which stand as guideposts to direct the user to the particular item in which the user is interested. Looseleaf Supplements     A special feature of this publication is the looseleaf system of binding and supplemental servicing of the publication. With this system, the publication will be kept up-to-date. Subsequent amendatory legislation will be properly edited, and the affected page or pages will be reprinted. These new pages will be distributed to holders of copies of the publication, with instructions for the manner of inserting the new pages and deleting the obsolete pages.     Keeping this publication up-to-date at all times will depend largely upon the holder of the publication. As revised pages are received, it will then become the responsibility of the holder to have the amendments inserted according to the attached instructions. It is strongly recommended by the publisher that all such amendments be inserted immediately upon receipt to avoid misplacing them and, in addition, that all deleted pages be saved and filed for historical reference purposes. Acknowledgments     This publication was under the direct supervision of Roger D. Merriam, Senior Code Attorney, and D. J. Heath, Editor, of the Municipal Code Corporation, Tallahassee, Florida. Credit is gratefully given to the other members of the publisher's staff for their sincere interest and able assistance throughout the project.     The publisher is most grateful to Ms. Charlotte Cotton, Chief Administrative Officer, Ms. Paula Martin, City Clerk, and Mr. James Skipper, City Attorney, for their cooperation and assistance during the progress of the work on this publication. It is hoped that their efforts and those of the publisher have resulted in a Code of Ordinances which will make the active law of the city readily accessible to all citizens and which will be a valuable tool in the day-to-day administration of the city's affairs. Copyright     All editorial enhancements of this Code are copyrighted by Municipal Code Corporation and the City of Americus, Georgia. Editorial enhancements include, but are not limited to: organization; table of contents; section catchlines; prechapter section analyses; editor's notes; state law references; numbering system; code comparative table; state law reference table; and index. Such material may not be used or reproduced for commercial purposes without the express written consent of Municipal Code Corporation and the City of Americus, Georgia. © ;hg;Copyrighted material. Municipal Code Corporation and the City of Americus, Georgia. 2007. 
Chapter 82 - SUBDIVISIONS 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
Sec. 82-1. - Definitions; street classifications.     The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:     Alleys means minor ways used primarily for vehicular services access to the rear or sides of commercial or industrial properties.     Collector streets means a street used to carry traffic from minor streets to major streets, including the principal entrance streets to a neighborhood or group development and streets for circulation within such neighborhood or development.     Streets are as defined in section 1-2, and for the purposes of these regulations, streets are classified as follows:     Major streets means a street used primarily for fast or heavy traffic.     Minor streets means a street used primarily for access to the abutting properties.     Subdivision. (1)  The term "subdivision" means any division of a tract or parcel of land into two or more lots, building sites or other divisions for the purpose, whether immediate or the future sale, legacy or building development, and includes any division of land involving a new street or a change in one or more existing streets and includes resubdivision and, where appropriate to the context, relates to the process of subdividing or to the land or area subdivided. (2)  Provided, however, the following are not included in this definition: a.  The subdivision of land for agricultural purposes provided no lot thereby produced is less than five acres or no new street is involved. b.  The sale or exchange of parcels of land between owners of adjoining properties, provided that additional lots are not thereby created, and that the lots created are in accordance with other city regulations. c.  The division of land into parcels where no new street is to be established and the resulting lots are equal to or larger than the standard required in the city, and a zoning classification of resulting lots remains the same as the zoning classification of the land before such division; provided, however, that nothing herein shall be construed to prevent the rezoning, of such property on proper application and approval granted in accordance with this Code. (Code 1986, § 19-1; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Sec. 82-2. - Zoning; conflict of standards. (a)  No final plat of land within the force and effect of an existing zoning regulations will be approved unless it conforms with such regulations. (b)  Whenever there is a discrepancy between minimum standards or building code, or other official standards, the highest standard shall apply. (Code 1986, § 19-38; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Sec. 82-3. - Variances.     Where the subdivider can show that a provision of these standards would cause unnecessary hardship if strictly adhered to, and where, because of topographical or other conditions peculiar to the site, in the opinion of the planning commission a departure may be made without destroying the intent of such provisions, the planning commission may authorize a variance. Any variance thus authorized is to be stated in writing in the minutes of the planning commission with the reasoning on which the departure was justified set forth. (Code 1986, § 19-39; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Sec. 82-4. - Enforcement—Authorities designated; duties.     The provisions of this chapter shall be administered and enforced by the community development director and the planning commission. The community development director shall: (1)  Receive all subdivision plats; (2)  In cooperation with the planning commission review and approve or disapprove subdivision plats; (3)  Inspect subdivisions for compliance with the requirement of this chapter and other applicable city ordinances. (Code 1986, § 19-2; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Sec. 82-5. - Same—Circumventing requirements; approval of plat required; access street required. (a)  The owner or agent of the owner of any land to be subdivided within the city who transfers or sells or agrees to sell negotiates to sell such land by reference to or exhibition of or by other use of a plat to subdivide such land before such plat has been approved by the planning commission and recorded in the office of the clerk of the superior court of this county, shall be denied all building permits, public services, and utility connections, and subject to punishment for ordinance violation and the description by metes and bounds in the instrument of transfer or other document used in the process of selling or transfer shall not exempt the transaction from such penalties. The city, through its attorney or other official designated by the city council, may enjoin such transfer or sale or agreement by appropriate action. (b)  No plat or plan of subdivision within the city shall be filed or recorded in the office of the clerk of the superior court of this county until it has been approved by the planning commission and such approval entered in writing on the plat by the secretary of the planning commission. (c)  No building permit shall be issued for and no building or other structure shall be erected on any lot within the city unless the street giving access to the lot upon which said building is proposed to be placed shall be accepted or opened as, or shall have otherwise received the legal status of a public street prior to that time, or unless such street corresponds in its location and line with a street shown on a subdivision plat approved by said planning commission or with a street located and accepted by the city. Any building erected in violation of this section shall be deemed an unlawful structure, and the building official, city attorney or other official designated by the city council may bring appropriate action to enjoin such erection or cause it to be vacated or removed. (Code 1986, § 19-3; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Sec. 82-6. - Preliminary plat filing fee.     The developer shall be assessed a filing fee in the amount established by ordinance payable to the finance director at the time of filing the preliminary plat. (Code 1986, § 19-4; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997; Ord. No. O-04-12-33, 12-16-2004) 
Secs. 82-7—82-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PROCEDURES FOR PLAT APPROVAL 
Sec. 82-31. - Generally. (a)  The procedure for formal review and approval of a subdivision plat shall consist of the following three separate steps: (1)  The subdivider should consult early and informally with the community development director and/or other city technical staff for advice and assistance before the preparation of the preliminary sketch plat and its formal application for approval. This will enable the subdivider to become thoroughly familiar with these standards, the major street plan and other official plans or public improvements that might affect the area. Such informal review should prevent unnecessary and costly revisions. (2)  Prior to the making of any street improvement, or installations of utilities, the developer shall submit to the planning commission a preliminary plat of the proposed subdivision. After receiving the planning commission's approval of the preliminary plat and full concurrence and approval by the city, the developer may then proceed to grade the streets and install all improvements required by this chapter and any other applicable city ordinances. In lieu of the completion of all improvements prior to submission of the final plat, the developer may post a bond with the city, or certified check, in an amount and with surety satisfactory to the city and conditions satisfactory to the city, providing for and securing to the city the actual construction and installation of such improvements within a period specified by the planning commission and stated in the bond. (3)  After completion of the physical development of the subdivision or the posting of a bond or certified check to guarantee the same, the developer shall submit to the planning commission a final plat together with any required certificates. The final plat, along with any deed restrictions, becomes the instrument to be recorded in the office of the clerk of the superior court of this county. (b)  No final subdivision plat shall be approved by the planning commission or accepted for record by the office of the clerk of the superior court of this county until the required improvements listed shall be constructed in satisfactory manner and approved by the appropriate approving agent. (Code 1986, § 19-20; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Sec. 82-32. - Preliminary plat. (a)  At least ten days prior to the regular meeting of the planning commission the subdivider shall submit to the building official's office three copies of the plat of the proposed subdivision drawn to a scale of not less than one inch equals 100 feet, along with a receipt for the filing fee from the finance director. (b)  The preliminary plat shall meet the minimum standards of design and general requirements for the construction of public improvements as set forth in article III of this chapter and shall give the following information insofar as possible: (1)  Description: a.  Proposed name of subdivision. b.  Name and address of subdivider. c.  Graphic scale, north point and date. The north point shall be identified as magnetic, true, or grid north. d.  Location sketch map showing the relationship of the subdivision site to the surrounding area, including directions and distances to readily identifiable landmarks in the surrounding area. e.  Acreage to be subdivided. (2)  Existing conditions: a.  Topography by contours at vertical intervals of not more than two feet, or as determined necessary by the city utilities director, when a new street is involved in a subdivision, including outline of wooded areas and classifications of land. b.  Zoning district classification on land to be subdivided and of adjoining land. c.  Names and addresses of adjoining property owners or subdivisions. d.  In case of resubdivision, a copy of existing plat with proposed resubdivision superimposed thereon. e.  Location of streams, lakes and swamps and land subject to flood as determined from past history of flooding (listed on appropriate FEMA map). f.  Location of existing and platted property lines, location, width and names of all platted roads, railroads, utility rights-of-way, public areas, existing buildings or structures. g.  Existing sewers, water mains, drains, culverts or other underground facilities within the tract or within the right-of-way of boundary roads, with sizes, grades and invert elevations from public records, or from field surveys, or other sources. All sizes and data on all utilities shall be provided. h.  Certification by the county health officer when individual sewage disposal or water systems are to be installed. (3)  Proposed conditions: a.  Layout of roads, alleys and public crosswalks, with widths, road names or designations. b.  Layout of all lots and the area of each lot, including building setback lines and lot divisions with scaled dimensions and utility easements with width and use on all lots. c.  Preliminary plan of all utilities to be constructed. d.  Designation of all land to be reserved or dedicated for public use. (c)  Within 30 days after submission of the preliminary plat, the planning commission shall review it and indicate its approval, disapproval, or approval subject to listed modifications, as a basis for preparation of the final plat. If a plat is disapproved, reasons for such disapproval will be stated in the records of the planning commission. Failure of the planning commission to act on the preliminary sketch within 30 days will be deemed approval of this plat, unless the developer agrees to an extension of time. (d)  Approval of the preliminary plat by the planning commission shall not constitute acceptance of the final plat and shall not be indicated on the preliminary plat. (e)  The approval of the preliminary plat shall lapse until a final plat based thereon is submitted within one year from the date of such approval, unless an extension of time is applied for and granted by the planning commission. (f)  After the planning commission has reviewed and acted on the preliminary plat, one copy will be returned to the developer, one copy will go to the building official's office and one copy will be retained in the records of the planning commission. (g)  After the planning commission has approved the preliminary plat, construction plans should be submitted to the building official and include the following: (1)  Layout of roads, alleys and public crosswalks, with widths, road names or designations, grades and cross sections. (2)  Preliminary plan of sanitary sewers with grades, service, pipe size and points of discharge, together with certified copy of all load design factors and computations. (3)  Preliminary plan of storm drainage system with glade, pipe size and location of outlet, together with certified copy of all design factors and computations. (4)  Preliminary plan of water supply system with pipe sizes and location of hydrants, valves and all appurtenances. (Code 1986, § 19-21; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997; Ord. No. O-04-12-33, 12-16-2004) 
Sec. 82-33. - Final plat. (a)  At least ten days prior to the regular meeting of the planning commission the subdivider shall submit to the building official's office an original on reproducible Mylar or vellum, and three copies, of the final plat. The final plat shall conform substantially to the preliminary plat as approved and, if desired by the subdivider, it may constitute only that portion of the preliminary plat which such developer proposes to record and develop at the time, provided, however, that such portion conforms to all requirements of these standards. (b)  The original shall be drawn to a scale of not less than one inch equals 100 feet on reproducible Mylar or vellum and shall correspond to plat book dimensions. It shall be the developer's responsibility to provide the clerk of superior court with a plat that will fit in the plat book/cabinet. When more than one sheet is required, an index sheet of the same size shall be filed showing the entire subdivision with sheets lettered in alphabetical order as a key. (c)  When the plat has been approved, the original will be returned to the developer with the approval of the planning commission certified thereon for filing with the clerk of the superior court of this county; one copy will be returned to the developer for such developer's records; one copy will be forwarded to the building official's office and one copy will be returned in the records of the planning commission. (d)  The planning commission shall approve or disapprove this final plat within 30 days after its submission to that body. Failure of the planning commission to act on this final plat within these 30 days shall be deemed approval of it. If the plat is disapproved, the grounds for disapproval shall be stated upon the records of the planning commission. (e)  Approval of the final plat by the planning commission shall not constitute acceptance by the public of the dedication of any streets or public ways or ground. (f)  The final plat shall comply with the plat act and shall give the following information: (1)  Certification that the applicant is the landowner, all parties with mortgage or lien interest to be included, and that applicant dedicates street rights-of-way and any sites for public use. (2)  Certification by a licensed surveyor to the accuracy of survey and plat and placement of monuments. (3)  Certification by the proper city officials that the developer has complied with the following: All improvements have been installed in accord with the requirements of this chapter and other applicable city ordinances. (4)  Protective covenants or deed restrictions, if any, shall be placed directly on the final plat or attached thereto in form for recording. (5)  Certificate on the plat to be signed by the secretary of the planning commission when the plat has been given final approval by the planning commission. (Code 1986, § 19-22; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997; Ord. No. O-99-02-08, 2-18-1999) 
Sec. 82-34. - As-built construction plans. (a)  The as-built construction plans shall give the following information: (1)  Sufficient information to reproduce the plat on the ground, including tract boundary lines and their relation to established land lot lines, right-of-way, property lines of residential lots, and other sites with accurate dimensions to the nearest one-hundredth of a foot, bearings, and angles on all lines, radii, arcs, and central angles of all curves with readings to the nearest minute. (2)  Profiles of grades for streets when required by the city. (3)  Blocks designated by letter and lots by number or lots numbered consecutively. (4)  Location and description of monuments. (5)  Final plan of sanitary sewers with grade, pipe sizes, and point of discharge. (6)  Final plan of storm drains with grade, pipe sizes, and point of discharge. (7)  Final plan of water supply system with pipe sites and location of hydrants and valves. (b)  The as-built construction plans shall be furnished to the public works department on a 3½-inch disk or CD and shall be in a .DWG or .DXF format. (Code 1986, § 19-23; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997; Ord. No. O-99-08-34, 8-19-1999) 
Secs. 82-35—82-56. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - REQUIREMENTS AND STANDARDS 
Sec. 82-57. - Basic requirements; minimum standards. (a)  Land which the planning commission has found to be unsuitable for subdivision due to flooding, bad drainage, steep slopes, rock formations, or other features likely to be harmful to the safety, health, and general welfare of the future residents shall not be subdivided unless adequate methods approved by the planning commission are formulated by the developer for meeting the problems created by the subdivision of such land. (b)  Land subject to flooding shall not be platted for residential occupancy or for such other uses, as will not comply with chapter 34, article II, the danger to health, life and property unless such land is not to be used as a building site. In applying this provision, land liable to flooding as determined from past history shall be considered subject to flood. Fill shall not be used to raise the land in areas subject to flood unless the fill proposed does not restrict the flow of water and unduly increase flood heights. (Code 1986, § 19-30; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Sec. 82-58. - Streets. (a)  Conformity to the major street plan. The location and width of all streets and roads shall conform to the official major street plan; i.e., provision must be made for the location of thoroughfares as shown on the major street plan. (b)  Relation to adjoining street system. The proposed street system shall extend existing streets at the same or greater width, but in no case less than the required minimum width. It shall connect with streets already dedicated in adjacent subdivisions or where no such streets exist, it shall follow the projection of streets in related subdivided tracts so that other subdivisions may connect therewith. The city reserves the right to require the developer to meet minimum road design standards. (c)  Restriction of access. When a tract fronts on an arterial street or highway, the planning commission may require all residential lots to be provided with frontage on a minor residential street. (d)  Street right-of-way widths. The minimum width of right-of-way, measured from lot line to lot line, shall be as shown on the major street plan, or if not shown on such plan, shall be not less than as follows: (1)  Arterial streets and highways: 80 to120 feet. (2)  Collector streets: 60 feet. (3)  Commercial and industrial streets: 80 feet. (4)  Minor residential streets: a.  Curb and gutter: 50 feet. b.  Ditches: 60 feet. For both of the above, a 15-foot utility drainage easement shall be provided on each side of the right-of-way. (e)  Exceptions. In cases where topography or other physical conditions made a street of the required minimum width impracticable, the planning commission may modify the above requirements. Through proposed business areas the street widths shall be increased ten feet on each side if needed to provide parking without interference to normal passing traffic. (f)  Additional width on existing street. Subdivisions that join existing streets shall dedicate additional rights-of-way if needed to meet the above minimum street width requirements. (1)  The entire right-of-way shall be provided where any part of the subdivision is on both sides of the existing street. (2)  When the subdivision is located on only one side of an existing street, one-half of the required right-of-way, measured from the centerline of the existing roadway shall be provided. (g)  Street grades and elevations. Grades on major streets shall not exceed seven percent and grades on other streets shall not exceed 12 percent. (h)  Horizontal curves. Where a deflection angle of more than two degrees in the alignment of a street occurs, a curve of reasonably long radius shall be introduced. On streets 60 feet or more in width, the centerline radius of curvature shall be not less than 300 feet; on other streets it shall not be less than 100 feet. (i)  Vertical curves. All changes in grade shall be connected by vertical curves of minimum length in feet equal to 15 times the algebraic difference in rates of grade for major streets, and one-half this minimum length for other streets. Profiles of all streets showing natural and finished grades drawn to a scale of not less than one inch equals 100 feet horizontally and one inch equals 20 feet vertically may be required by the planning commission upon recommendation of the city utilities director. (j)  Intersections. Street intersections shall be as nearly at right angles as possible, and no intersection shall be at an angle of less than 60 degrees. Property line radii at street intersections shall not be less than 20 feet, and where the angle of street intersection is less than 75 degrees the planning commission may require a greater curb radius. To permit the construction of a curb having a desirable radius without curtailing the sidewalk at a street corner to less than normal width, the property line at such street corner shall be reduced or otherwise set back sufficiently to permit such construction. (k)  Tangents. A tangent of at least 100 feet long shall be introduced between reverse curves on all streets. (l)  Street jogs. Street jogs with centerline offsets of less than 125 feet shall not be allowed. (m)  Dead-end streets. (1)  Minor terminal streets or courts designed to have one end permanently closed shall be no more than 600 feet long unless necessitated by topography. They shall be provided at the closed end with a turnaround having an outside roadway diameter of at least 90 feet and a street right-of-way diameter of at least 110 feet for curb and gutter and 130 feet for ditches. (2)  Where phases may be proposed a temporary turnaround shall be provided. (n)  Private streets and reserve strips. There shall be no private streets platted in any subdivision. Every lot of subdivided property shall be served from a publicly dedicated street. There shall be no reserve strips controlling access to streets, except where the control of such strips is definitely placed with the city under conditions approved by the planning commission. (o)  Street names. Proposed streets that are obviously, in alignment with others already existing and named shall bear the names of existing streets. In no case shall the names for proposed streets duplicate names of existing streets, irrespective of the use of the suffix "street," "avenue," "boulevard," "driveway," "place" or "court." (p)  Alleys. Alleys shall be provided to the rear of all lots used for business purposes; alleys shall not be provided in residential blocks except where the subdivider produces evidence satisfactory to the planning commission of the need for alleys. (q)  Construction requirements. (1)  Every subdivision developer shall be required to make adequate provision for handling drainage problems, to grade and improve streets and alleys, to install curbs or invert ditches and to install street name signs in accordance with specifications established by the city utilities director. (2)  All street design and construction and related matters shall be in strict accordance with Georgia Department of Transportation Standard Specifications, volume 1 "Construction of Roads and Bridges" and volume 2 "Materials for Roads and Bridges" and all revisions thereto. Where circumstances dictate variations from the standard specifications, the city utilities director may vary the requirements providing the design or materials accepted are in all ways commensurate with good practice. (3)  All materials, equipment, labor and other matters related to street construction shall be provided by the developer. The following is a summary of the improvements required: a.  Grading. All streets, roads and alleys shall be graded to their full width by the subdivider so that pavements and sidewalks, if installed in the future can be constructed on the same level plane. The preparation of the right-of-way before grading is started and the construction of cuts and fills shall be accomplished according to the specifications of the city. b.  Storm drainage. An adequate drainage system, including necessary curbs, pipes, culverts, headwalls, intersectional drains, drop inlets, bridges, swale ditches, etc., shall be provided for the proper drainage of all surface water. c.  Installation of utilities. After grading is completed and approved and before any base is applied all of the underground work (water mains, gas mains, etc. and all service connections) shall be installed completely and approved throughout the length of the road and across the flat section. All driveways for houses to be built by the developer shall be cut and drained. d.  Roadway base. After preparation of the subgrade, the roadbed shall be properly based with one of the following: 1.  A six-inch sand clay base (class B); 2.  A six-inch graded aggregate base; or 3.  Six-inch mixed in place soil cement base. e.  Roadway surfacing. The paved surface shall be a two-inch compacted asphalt plant mix. f.  Minimum pavement width. Minimum pavement including paved gutters between curbs shall be as follows: 1.  Minor residential streets: 30 feet. 2.  Access routes: 38 to 44 feet. 3.  Arterial streets or through routes: As may be required. 4.  Ditch sections: 24 feet. g.  Curbs. Where the subdivider elects to provide curbs or it is deemed essential and necessary by the city utilities director, a permanent six-inch Portland cement concrete curb and gutter with a longitudinal storm drain system shall be installed. Backfill shall slope toward the curb to ensure drainage of surface water into the storm drainage system. h.  Rural ditch section. Where the developer does not install curb and gutter, a rural ditch section shall be provided. Said ditch shall be constructed with a minimum of 3:1 slope on both sides of the ditch. And shall have a minimum channel width of at least two feet. All rural ditch sections shall be designed and constructed to accommodate a 25-year flood. No rural ditch section shall be constructed within a right-of-way less than 60 feet wide with a 15-foot utility/storm drainage easement, on both sides. All rural ditch sections shall be seeded or sodded to provide for a permanent stand of grass. i.  Outfall ditches. Outfall ditches shall be piped 130 feet from the right-of-way. (Code 1986, § 19-31; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Sec. 82-59. - Blocks. (a)  In general, blocks shall be not less than 400 feet, nor more than 1,200 feet in length, except where topography or other conditions peculiar to the site make such dimensions impracticable. (b)  Blocks shall be wide enough to allow two tiers of lots of minimum depth, except where fronting on major streets or prevented by topography conditions or size of the property, in which case the planning commission will approve a single tier or lots of minimum depth. (Code 1986, § 19-32; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Sec. 82-60. - Lots. (a)  Arrangement. Insofar as practical, side lot lines shall be at right angles to straight street lines or radial to curved street lines. Each lot shall front upon a public street or road that is not less than 50 feet in width. Each lot shall be at least 30 feet in width at the front property line. (b)  Minimum size. The size, shape and orientation of lots shall be such, as the planning commission deems appropriate for the type of development and use contemplated. Where a public sanitary sewer is reasonably accessible, the subdivider shall connect with such sewer and provide a connection to each lot. Where a public sewer is not accessible, an alternate method of sewage disposal may be used when meeting all applicable public health regulations. (1)  Residential lots served by a public sewer system shall be not less than 60 feet wide at the building setback line, nor less than 7,000 square feet in area. Where a rural ditch section is used, each lot shall maintain a 100-foot width at the setback line, not less than 13,000 square feet in size, and maintain a minimum frontage at the right-of-way line of 50 feet. Where a cul-de-sac is constructed using the rural ditch section method, the maximum number of lots on a cul-de-sac shall be five lots, with a minimum right-of-way diameter of 130 feet, and a minimum paving diameter being 90 feet. (2)  For residential lots not served by a public sewer system, the planning commission shall require that data from percolation tests be submitted as a basis for approving subdivisions dependent upon septic tanks as a means of sewage disposal, and no lot shall be less than 100 feet wide at the building line, nor less than 15,000 square feet in area. (3)  For residential lots not served by a public water supply or a public sewer system, no lot shall be less than 100 feet wide at the building line, nor less than one acre in size except upon approval of the county health officer and in no case shall any lot be less than one-half acre in size. (4)  The minimum size of residential lots to be served by a private source of water supply shall be determined by the county health officer after investigations of soil conditions, proposed sewer system and depth of groundwater. (5)  Size of properties reserved or laid out for commercial or industrial properties shall be adequate to provide for the off-street service and parking facilities required by the type of use and development contemplated. Platting of individual lots shall be avoided in favor of an overall design of the land to be used for such purposes. (6)  The size and widths of lots shall in no case be less than the minimum requirements of the zoning regulations in effect. (c)  Building setback lines. The minimum depth of building setback lines from any street shall be 30 feet. If, however, suitable provision is made in connection with the plat or restrictions pertaining to the plat, building lines may be varied, provided such variation does not reduce the setback more than five feet. Where rural ditch section construction for a subdivision is used the minimum building setback line from any street right-of-way shall be 50 feet for any zoning district. (d)  Corner lots. Corner lots shall be sufficiently wider and larger to permit the additional side yard requirements of the zoning regulations or building setback lines outlined above. (Code 1986, § 19-33; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Sec. 82-61. - Utilities. (a)  Water. Water mains for both domestic use and fire protection shall be properly connected with the city water system. The lines shall conform with accepted standards of good practice for municipal water systems, and shall meet, as a minimum, the requirements of the state environmental protection division and the city. All materials, labor, equipment, and other matters related to the water distribution system shall be provided by the developer. (b)  Sewer. When the subdivision is located within the service area of a public sewer system, sanitary sewers shall be installed in such a manner as to serve adequately all lots with connection to the public system. Where lots cannot be economically connected with a sewer system, they must contain adequate area for the installation of approved septic tank and disposal fields and must be approved in writing by the county health officer. All materials, equipment, labor, and other matters related to the sanitary sewer system shall be provided by the developer and all sewer facilities shall be installed in accordance with the standards of the department of human resources of the state and standards of the city. (c)  Installation of utilities. After grading is completed and approved and before any base is applied to the street, all of the underground work, water mains, gas mains, etc., and all service connections shall be installed completed and approved throughout the length of the road and across the flat section. Where the utility mains are off the pavement, the developer may elect to omit the installation of service connections providing that at such time as these service connections are needed, they may be jacked across the street without breaking or weakening the existing pavement. (d)  Easements for utilities. Except where alleys are permitted for that purpose, the city may require easements for poles, wires, conduits, storm and sanitary sewers, gas, and water mains or other utility lines, along rear lot lines or side lot lines, if, in the opinion of the city utilities director such action is desirable. Easements of the same or greater width may be required along the line of or across lots, where necessary for the extension of existing or planned utilities. Where a subdivision is traversed by a watercourse, drainageway, channel or stream, there shall be provided a stormwater easement or drainage right-of-way along each side for the purpose of widening, depending, relocating, improving or protecting such drainage easement. (e)  Street lighting. Either underground or overhead electrical service shall be provided by the developer of a subdivision, through a public utility. All subdivisions with underground electrical lines shall have placed appropriate utility poles for street lighting. The installation of streetlights shall adhere to the following requirements: streetlights shall be installed at each street intersection and streetlights that are to be installed along the proposed blocks shall be equally spaced between street intersections. However, the maximum distance between any two streetlights shall not exceed 400 feet in length. After construction has been completed for an accepted phase or for an entire subdivision, and where the streets have been dedicated to the city, the city will be responsible for the costs associated with the operation of the streetlights. Streetlight design, size, and wattage must be approved by the city as part of the preliminary platting process. For example, a block 800 feet in length, it would be necessary to install three streetlights. For a block 1,100 feet in length, four streetlights would be necessary. (Code 1986, § 19-34; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Sec. 82-62. - Monuments.     Concrete monuments four inches in diameter or square, four feet long, with a flat top, shall be set at all street corners at all points where the street lines intersect the exterior boundaries of the subdivision, and at angle points and points of curve in each street. The top of the monument shall have an indented cross to identify properly the location and shall be set flush with the finished grade. All other lot, corners shall be marked with iron pipe not less than three-fourths inches in diameter and 24 inches long and driven so as to be flush with the finished grade. (Code 1986, § 19-35; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Sec. 82-63. - Large tracts.     When land is subdivided into larger parcels than ordinary building lots, such parcels shall be arranged so as to allow for the opening of future streets and logical further resubdivision. (Code 1986, § 19-36; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Sec. 82-64. - Group housing developments.     A comprehensive group housing development, including the large scale construction of housing units together with necessary drives and ways of access, may be approved by the planning commission although the design of the project does not include standard street, lot and subdivision arrangements, if departure from the foregoing standards can be made without destroying their intent. The developer shall provide proof that adequate access is provided for emergency vehicles. (Code 1986, § 19-37; Ord. No. O-97-03-05, 3-20-1997) 
Chapter 86 - TRAFFIC AND VEHICLES[1] Footnotes: --- (1) --- State Law reference— Traffic generally, O.C.G.A. § 40-1-1 et seq.; power of local authorities generally, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-371; adoption of uniform rules of the road by local authorities, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-372. 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
Sec. 86-1. - State law—Adoption by reference.     Pursuant to chapter 6 of title 40 of the Official Code of Georgia Annotated (Code §§ 40-6-372—40-6- 376, Code §§ 40-6-1—40-6-397) of that chapter known as the Uniform Rules of the Road, and the definitions contained in O.C.G.A. § 40-1-1, are hereby adopted as and for the traffic regulations of the City of Americus with like effect as if recited herein. (Code 1962, § 23-152(a); Code 1986, § 20-1; Ord. No. O-2013-4, § 1, 2-21-2013) 
Sec. 86-2. - Same—Penalty.     Unless another penalty is expressly provided by law, every person convicted of a violation of any provision of this article shall be punished as provided in section 1-8 of this Code. (Code 1962, § 23-153; Code 1986, § 20-2; Ord. No. O-2013-4, § 2, 2-21-2013) 
Sec. 86-3. - Riding on outside of vehicle.     It shall be unlawful for any person to ride on the fenders, bumpers or any other portion of any motor vehicle, except on the inside thereof. (Code 1962, § 23-27; Code 1986, § 20-30) 
Secs. 86-4—86-24. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
Sec. 86-25. - Authority of police and fire department officials. (a)  It shall be the duty of the officers of the police department or such officers as are assigned by the chief of police to enforce this chapter and all other traffic laws of this city and all of the state vehicle laws applicable to street traffic in this city. (b)  Officers of the police department, or such officers as are assigned by the chief of police, are hereby authorized to direct all traffic by voice, hand, or signal in conformity with traffic laws, provided, that in the event of a fire or other emergency or to expedite traffic or to safeguard pedestrians, officers of the police department may direct traffic as conditions may require notwithstanding the provisions of the traffic laws. (c)  Officers of the fire department, when at the scene of a fire, may direct or assist the police in directing traffic threat or in the immediate vicinity. (Code 1962, § 23-9; Code 1986, § 20-4) 
Sec. 86-26. - Authority of chief of police to delegate power and duties.     The chief of police shall have the power to delegate to any other officer in the police department the duties and responsibilities conferred on such chief by this chapter. (Code 1962, § 23-10; Code 1986, § 20-5) 
Sec. 86-27. - Authority of utilities director. (a)  Signs on one-way streets. Whenever this chapter or any ordinance of this city designates any one-way street or alley, the utilities director shall place and maintain signs giving notice thereof, and no such regulation shall be effective unless such signs are in place. Signs indicating the direction of lawful traffic movement shall be placed at every intersection where movement of traffic in the opposite direction is prohibited. (b)  Speed signs. The police chief shall cause to be erected and the utilities director shall erect throughout the city signs indicating the maximum speed limit and/or such other information as will be informative to drivers of motor vehicles as it pertains to traffic control regulations at said location or in the city. (c)  Turn signs. The police chief is hereby authorized to determine those intersections at which drivers of vehicles shall not make a right or left turn. The utilities director shall place proper signs at such intersections. The making of such turns may be prohibited between certain hours of any day and permitted at other hours, in which event the same shall be plainly indicated on the signs, or they may be removed when such turns are permitted. (d)  Turn markers. The utilities director is authorized to place markers, buttons, and signs within or adjacent to intersections indicating the course to be traveled by vehicles turning at such intersection, and such course to be traveled as so indicated may conform to or be other than as prescribed by this chapter or other law or ordinance. (e)  Marking crosswalks, safety zones, traffic lanes. The utilities director is hereby authorized: (1)  To designate and maintain, by appropriate devices, marks or lines upon the surface of the roadway, crosswalks at intersections where there is particular danger to pedestrians crossing the roadway and at such other places as such engineer may deem necessary. (2)  To establish safety zones of such kind and character and at such places as may be necessary for the protection of pedestrians. (3)  To make lanes for traffic on street pavements at such places as may be advisable, consistent with this chapter and other traffic ordinances of the city. (f)  Stop signs. Whenever this chapter or any ordinance of the city designates and describes a through street it shall be the duty of the utilities director to place and maintain a stop sign or yield right-of-way sign on each intersection of such through street or intersection of that portion described and designated as such by this chapter or any ordinance of this city. (g)  Hazardous locations. The police chief is hereby authorized to determined and designate intersections where particular hazards exist upon streets other than those designated by this chapter or any other ordinance of this city as through streets, and to place at such determined and designated hazardous intersections at one or more entrances to any such intersection either a stop sign or yield right-of-way sign. (Code 1962, §§ 23-12, 23-32, 23-54, 23-55, 23-64, 23-118, 23-119; Code 1986, § 20-6; Ord. No. O-92-03-15, 3-23-1992) 
Sec. 86-28. - Temporary traffic rules.     Where the traffic upon the streets becomes congested, and upon occasions of parades, at theaters and other public places where large numbers of vehicles are assembled, the police may make temporary rules regulating the traffic in such congested districts. (Code 1962, § 23-62; Code 1986, § 20-17) 
Sec. 86-29. - Play streets; authority to establish.     The police chief shall have authority to declare any street or part thereof a play street and to place appropriate signs or devices in the roadway indicating and helping to protect the same. (Code 1962, § 23-71; Code 1986, § 20-40; Ord. No. O-92-03-15, 3-23-1992) 
Secs. 86-30—86-46. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - VIOLATIONS AND PENALTIES 
Sec. 86-47. - Owner liable for parking violation.     It shall be unlawful for any person to allow, permit, or suffer any vehicle registered in such person's name to stand or park in any street, in violation of this chapter or any other ordinance of the city regulating the parking of vehicles. Such person shall be equally liable with the operator for such violation and in addition thereto may have the vehicle impounded; provided, however, this shall not apply in those instances described in O.C.G.A. § 40-6-207. (Code 1962, § 23-144; Code 1986, § 20-80) 
Sec. 86-48. - Presumption in reference to illegal parking. (a)  In any prosecution charging a violation of any law or regulation governing the standing or parking of a vehicle proof that the particular vehicle described in the complaint was parked in violation of any such law or regulation, together with proof that the defendant named in the complaint was at the time of such parking the registered owner of such vehicle, shall constitute in evidence a prima facie presumption that the registered owner of such vehicle was the person who parked or placed such vehicle at the point where, and for the time which, such violation occurred; provided, however, this shall not apply in those instances described in O.C.G.A. § 40-6-207. (b)  The foregoing stated presumption shall apply only when the procedure in section 86-49 has been followed. (Code 1962, § 23-142; Code 1986, § 20-81) 
Sec. 86-49. - Notice on illegally parked vehicle.     Whenever any motor vehicle without a driver is found parked or stopped in violation of any of the restrictions imposed by this chapter or other ordinance of this city or by state law, the officer finding such vehicle shall take its registration number and may take other information displayed on the vehicle which may identify its user, and shall conspicuously affix to such vehicle a notice in writing, on a form provided by the city clerk for the driver to answer to the charge at the time and place specified in the notice. (Code 1962, § 23-143; Code 1986, § 20-82) 
Sec. 86-50. - When summons for arrest to be issued.     In the event any person fails to comply with a notice given to such person or attached to a vehicle or fails to make appearance pursuant to a summons, or if any person fails or refuses to deposit bail as required and within the time permitted by ordinance, the city clerk shall forthwith secure and issue a summons for such person's arrest. (Code 1962, § 23-146; Code 1986, § 20-83) 
Sec. 86-51. - When warrants for arrest to be issued.     When it shall be made to appear to the municipal court that any person has been lawfully served with a copy of charges to appear in such court for trial and shall fail to appear at the time and place set forth in such copy of charges, it shall be the duty of the municipal judge to forthwith issue a warrant for the arrest of such person and deliver same to the chief of police. (Code 1962, § 23-150; Code 1986, § 20-86) 
Secs. 86-52—86-75. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - VEHICLE OPERATION 
Sec. 86-76. - Maximum speed limits—Generally.     Motor vehicles shall not be driven at a higher rate of speed than 30 miles per hour in the city, nor a higher rate of speed than ten miles per hour in any park or cemetery owned and maintained by the city. (Code 1962, § 23-28; Code 1986, § 20-31) State Law reference— Speed limits generally, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-181. 
Sec. 86-77. - Same—In school zones.     It shall be unlawful for any person to drive a motor vehicle on streets adjoining school property during school days, in excess of 15 miles per hour. (Code 1962, § 23-31; Code 1986, § 20-32) 
Sec. 86-78. - Speed zones established.     The following speed zones are established for vehicles upon the following streets within the corporate limits of the city, as follows: (1)  On-system. Signs to be erected by the state department of transportation: a.  State Route 3 from the south city limits (Mile Point 10.62) to a point 500 feet south of McGarrah Street (Mile Point 11.82), a distance of 1.20 miles, to be zoned for 45 miles per hour. b.  State Route 3 from a point 500 feet south of McGarrah Street (Mile Point 11.82) to State Route 30 (Mile Point 12.24), a distance of 0.42 miles, to be zoned for 35 miles per hour. c.  State Route 3 from State Route 30 (Mile Point 12.24) to north city limits (Mile Point 13.08), a distance of 0.84 miles, to be zoned for 45 miles per hour. d.  State Route 27 (Lamar Street) from State Route 3 (Mile Point 12.53) to Dudley Street (Mile Point 12.90), a distance of 0.37 miles, to be zoned for 35 miles per hour. e.  State Route 27 Street (Mile Point 13.32) to State Route 30 (Presidential Route) (Mile Point 14.63), a distance of 1.31 miles, to be zoned for 35 miles per hour. g.  State Route 27 (Lamar Street) from State Route 30 (Presidential Route) (Mile Point 14.63) to east city limits (Mile Point 14.88), a distance of 0.25 miles, to be zoned for 45 miles per hour. h.  State Route 27 Dual (Forsyth Street) from State Route 27 (Lamar Street) (Mile Point 0.00) to State Route 49 (Mile Point 0.65), a distance of 0.65 miles, to be zoned for 45 miles per hour. i.  State Route 27 Dual (Forsyth Street) from State Route 49 (Mile Point 0.65) to Price Street (Mile Point 1.41), a distance of 0.76 miles, to be zoned for 35 miles per hour. j.  State Route 27 Dual (Forsyth Street) from Prince Street (Mile Point 1.41) to Dudley Street (Mile Point 1.83), a distance of 0.42 miles, to be zoned for 25 miles per hour. k.  State Route 27 Dual (Forsyth Street) from Dudley Street (Mile Point 1.83) to State Route 3 (Mile No. O-87-04-07, 4-27-1987; Ord. No. O-92-03-16, 3-23-1992; Ord. No. O-95-01-01, 1-26-1995; Ord. No. O-95-06-22, 6-22-1995; Ord. No. O-96-03-13, 3-21-1996; Ord. No. O-98-11-39, 11-19-1998; Ord. No. O-02-07-18, 7-18-2002; Ord. No. O-03-09-24, 9-18-2003; Ord. No. O-04-01-03, 1-22-2004; Ord. No. O-04-10-20, 10-21-2004; Ord. No. O-04-11-24, 11-18-2004) State Law reference— Local alteration of speed limits, O.C.G.A. §§ 40-6-9, 40-6-183. 
Sec. 86-79. - Driving in a procession generally.     Each driver in a funeral or other procession shall drive as near to the right-hand edge of the street or roadway as practicable and shall follow the vehicle ahead as close as is practicable and safe. (Code 1962, § 23-42; Code 1986, § 20-35) 
Sec. 86-80. - Vehicles comprising funeral procession. (a)  Vehicles of a funeral procession shall have the right-of-way over all other vehicles, except authorized emergency vehicles, provided each shall identify itself by burning regular headlights, and by keeping in close formation. (b)  When the lead vehicle in a funeral procession has entered an intersection on a green light, all other cars in the procession may proceed through the intersection, even though such signal may change to red. (Code 1962, § 23-34; Code 1986, § 20-36) 
Sec. 86-81. - Driving through funeral or other procession.     No driver of a vehicle shall drive between the vehicles comprising a funeral or other authorized procession while they are in motion and when such vehicles are conspicuously designated as required in section 86-80. (Code 1962, § 23-41; Code 1986, § 20-37) 
Sec. 86-82. - Signal to leave parking space.     Whenever vehicles are parked parallel to the curbing, before the operator of a parked vehicle or a vehicle stopped or standing at the edge of the street or roadway as prescribed in this chapter, shall execute a movement into any portion of the street or roadway normally used for moving traffic, such person shall signal the intention to do so by first giving the signal as prescribed in O.C.G.A. §§ 40-6-123—40-6-125, and shall start such movement only when the operator can do so with reasonable safety and without creating a hazard to other traffic moving lawfully within the street or roadway. (Code 1962, § 23-38; Code 1986, § 20-39) State Law reference— Starting parked vehicle, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-122. 
Sec. 86-83. - Designated play streets.     Whenever authorized signs are erected indicating any street or part thereof as a play street, no person shall drive a vehicle upon any such street or portion thereof except drivers of vehicles having business or whose residences are within such closed area, and then any such driver shall exercise the highest degree of care in driving upon any such street or portion thereof, and at no time shall such driver's speed exceed five miles per hour. (Code 1962, § 23-40; Code 1986, § 20-41) 
Sec. 86-84. - Towing.     No vehicle shall tow more than one other vehicle, nor shall the connection between vehicles exceed 16 feet in length. (Code 1962, § 23-45; Code 1986, § 20-43) 
Sec. 86-85. - Vehicle colliding with object.     No driver of any vehicle shall operate same, in such manner so as to collide with any object legally placed upon or adjacent to any street or highway. (Code 1962, § 23-47; Code 1986, § 20-44) 
Sec. 86-86. - Vehicle involved in collision with parked vehicle.     No driver of any vehicle shall operate same, in such a manner so as to collide with any vehicle properly parked. (Code 1962, § 23-49; Code 1986, § 20-45) 
Sec. 86-87. - Vehicle leaving street or roadway.     No driver of any vehicle shall operate same, in such a manner as to enter or leave any street or highway except at an intersection or at an alley or private drive. (Code 1962, § 23-48; Code 1986, § 20-46) 
Sec. 86-88. - One-way streets. (a)  East and west. Traffic upon the streets designated shall move as follows in one direction only: (1)  On Forsyth Street in a westerly direction from the Vienna Road to Highway 19. (2)  On Lamar Street in an easterly direction from Highway 19 to the Vienna Road. (3)  On East Peppermint Way in an easterly direction from its intersection with North Lee Street to its intersection with Montgomery Street. (b)  North. (1)  Between Forsyth Street to the north and Forsyth Street to the south, traffic upon the following street shall be one-way north: Windsor Avenue. (2)  Jones Lane, from its intersection with Patterson Street to its intersection with Peppermint Way, shall be a one-way street in a northerly direction. (3)  Oak Avenue from Glessner Street to Bell Street shall be a one-way street in a northerly direction on Friday nights when Americus High School is hosting home football games. (c)  South. (1)  On Harrold Avenue, traffic shall be one-way south from Bell Street to Glessner Street from 7:00 a.m. until 8:30 a.m. during the time that Americus High School is in session. (2)  On Harrold Avenue, traffic shall be one-way south from Bell Street to Glessner Street from 3:00 p.m. until 4:30 p.m. during the times that Americus High School is in session. (d)  West. (1)  Peppermint Way between North Jackson Street and North Lee Street shall be a one-way street in a westerly direction. (2)  Sheffield Street from Quincy Drive to Jackson Street shall be a one-way street in a westerly direction. (3)  Glessner Street from Harrold Avenue to Oak Avenue shall be a one-way street in a westerly direction on Friday nights when Americus High School is hosting home football games. (e)  Other streets. Traffic on all other streets, unless otherwise indicated, shall be two-way traveling in both directions. (Code 1962, § 23-58; Code 1986, § 20-48; Ord. No. O-96-08-33, 8-22-1996; Ord. No. O-02-02-07, 2-21-2002; Ord. No. O-03-09-26, 9-18-2003; Ord. No. O-04-07-13, 7-22-2004; O-2012-13, 5-24-2012) State Law reference— Authority to establish one-way streets, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-371(a)(4); one-way streets, O.C.G.A. § 49-6-47. 
Sec. 86-89. - Stop when traffic obstructed.     No driver shall enter an intersection or a marked crosswalk unless there is sufficient space on the other side of the intersection or crosswalk to accommodate the vehicle he is operating without obstructing the passage of other vehicles or pedestrians, notwithstanding any traffic control signal indication to proceed. (Code 1962, § 23-120; Code 1986, § 20-49) 
Sec. 86-90. - Criminal trespass by a motor vehicle. (a)  A person commits the offense of criminal trespass by a motor vehicle when the person, after having been requested not to do so by a law enforcement officer or by the owner or an authorized agent of the owner, parks or stands an occupied or unoccupied motor vehicle in, or repeatedly drives a motor vehicle through or within, a parking area which is located on privately owned property and is provided by a merchant, a group of merchants, or a shopping center or other similar facility for customers if: (1)  The parking area identified by at least one sign as specified in this section, and if the parking area contains more than 150 parking spaces then by at least one such sign for every 150 parking spaces, each sign containing the following information in easy-to-read printing: a.  Notice of the elements of the crime of criminal trespass by motor vehicle; b.  Identification of the property that is reserved for customers' use only; c.  Identification of the merchant, group of merchants, or shopping center or other similar facility providing the parking area; and d.  Warning that violators will be prosecuted. (2)  The motor vehicle is parked, is standing, or is being operated other than for the purpose of: a.  Transporting some person to or from the interior of the place of business of a merchant identified by the sign or signs in the parking area, or to or from the interior of the shopping center or other facility so identified; b.  Making use of a telephone, vending machine, automatic teller machine, or other similar facility located in the parking area; c.  Meeting the requirements of a situation in which it has unexpectedly become impossible or impractical for the motor vehicle to continue to travel on the public roads; or d.  Carrying out an activity for which express permission has been given by the owner of the parking area of an authorized representative of the owner. (b)  Any person violating this section shall be subject to a monetary fine as follows: (1)  Not to exceed $50.00 for the first such violation; (2)  Not to exceed $100.00 for the second such violation; (3)  Not to exceed $150.00 for the third or subsequent such violation. (Code 1986, § 20-50; Ord. No. O-87-06-11, 6-22-1987) State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-252. 
Sec. 86-91. - Four-way stop intersections.     There shall be established and enforced a four-way stop traffic regulation at the following intersections: (1)  Oglethorpe Avenue and Jefferson Street. (2)  Freida Lane and Jefferson Street. (3)  Douglas Circle and Ridge Street. (4)  Hancock Avenue and Bell Street. (5)  Lorraine Avenue and Peggy Ann Drive. (6)  Edgewood Avenue and Anthony Drive. (7)  Hancock Street and Furlow Street. (8)  Harrold Street and Furlow Street. (9)  Hill Street and Jackson Street. (10)  Hill Street and Harrold Avenue. (11)  Hancock Street and Hill Street. (12)  Douglas Drive and Pinecrest Drive. (13)  Jackson Avenue and Furlow Street. (14)  North Jackson Street with J. R. Campbell Drive. (15)  Alice Street and John Street. (Code 1986, § 20-51; Ord. No. O-87-06-13, 6-22-1987; Ord. No. O-89-6-17, 6-26-1989; Ord. No. O-89-7-23, 7-24-1989; Ord. No. O-91-07-23(a), 7-29-1991; Ord. No. O-91-10-36, 10-28-1991; Ord. No. O-96-03-11, 3-21-1996; Ord. No. O-98-11-41, 11-19-1998; Ord. No. O-99-04-16, 4-22-1999; Ord. No. O-99-11-45, 11-18-1999; Ord. No. O-05-07-17, 7-21-2005; Ord. No. O-07-08-23, 8-23-2007; Ord. No. O-07-08-24, 8-23-2007; Ord. No. O-11-12-31, 12-15-2011) State Law reference— Authority to regulate or prohibit stopping, standing or parking, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-371(a)(1). 
Sec. 86-92. - Three-way stop intersections.     There shall be established and enforced a three-way stop traffic regulation at the following intersections: (1)  Church Street and Brown Street. (2)  East Jefferson Street and Oglethorpe Avenue. (3)  GSW State University Drive and Wheatley Street. (4)  Taylor Street and Barlow Street. (Code 1986, § 20-52; Ord. No. O-00-07-31, 7-20-2000; Ord. No. O-04-02-04, 2-19-2004; Ord. No. O-06-04-11, 4-20-2006; Ord. No. O-07-09-31, 9-20-2007) State Law reference— Authority to regulate or prohibit stopping, standing or parking, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-371(a)(1). 
Sec. 86-93. - One-way stop intersections.     There shall be established and enforced a one-way stop at the intersection of East Jefferson Street and Oglethorpe Street in the city. The existing stop signs requiring a stop on Oglethorpe Avenue shall be removed. The city shall be authorized to install signage preceding the new stop sign advising motorists that the traffic on Oglethorpe Avenue traveling both east and west shall not be required to stop at such intersection. (Ord. No. O-10-11-40, 11-18-2010) 
Sec. 86-94. - Two-way stop intersections.     There shall be established and enforced a two-way stop traffic regulation at the following intersections: (1)  North Jackson Street and Tom Hall Circle. (Ord. No. O-12-04-08, 4-19-2012)

ARTICLE IV. - STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING[2] Footnotes: --- (2) --- State Law reference— Stopping, standing and parking, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-200 et seq.; authority to regulate or prohibit stopping, standing or parking, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-371(a)(1). 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
Sec. 86-113. - Park within markings. (a)  It shall be unlawful to park any vehicle on any portion of the streets within the city that have been or are, at the time of such parking, marked in sections indicating by such marking where and how vehicles shall be parked, otherwise than in conformity to such markings, leaving all the wheels of such parked vehicle clearly within the space indicated by such marks for parking of vehicles. (b)  The provisions of this section shall not apply to commercial vehicles over 25 feet in length delivering or receiving cargo from buildings not equipped with off-street loading and unloading capabilities, providing said vehicles park in such manner for no more than 15 minutes, block only one lane of traffic, and that such vehicle is moved upon demand of any motorist whose exit from parking may be blocked by the delivery vehicle. (Code 1962, § 23-79; Code 1986, § 20-60; Ord. No. O-92-06-18, 6-22-1992) 
Sec. 86-114. - Parking in alley.     It shall be unlawful for any driver or operator of any vehicle to park the same in any public alley within the city except where such motor vehicles are being loaded or unloaded or are awaiting loading or unloading of wares, goods or merchandise from or to the buildings or adjacent property to be served by said alley. (Code 1962, § 23-82; Code 1986, § 20-61) 
Sec. 86-115. - Parking of certain tractor-trailer rigs on residential streets.     No tractor-trailer rig or motor vehicle with a gross vehicle weight of 21,000 pounds or more shall be parked on a public street within the city, which public street has adjoining property which is zoned R-1 district or R-2 district. (Code 1962, § 23-83; Code 1986, § 20-62) 
Sec. 86-116. - Parking spaces for disabled in downtown. (a)  There is hereby established parking spaces in the downtown area of the city for use by persons with disabilities such parking spaces to be located as follows: (1)  On the west side of Jackson Avenue in the space immediately north of the cross walk; (2)  On the south side of Forsyth Street in the space immediately east of Windsor Avenue. (b)  The police chief, or his designee, shall be authorized to acquire and install appropriate signage at such parking spaces to indicate that they are reserved for the use of disabled citizens in accord with this section. (Code 1986, § 20-63; Ord. No. O-92-08-26, 8-24-1992) 
Sec. 86-117. - Report of violation; fine. (a)  In each violation of this article, it shall be the duty of the police officers to report to the chief of police: (1)  The state license of such vehicle. (2)  The time of day or night the officer detected such violation of the provisions of this article. (3)  Any other facts, knowledge of which is necessary to a thorough understanding of the circumstances attending such violation. (b)  Each police officer shall also attach to such vehicle a notice to the owner or operator thereof that such vehicle has been parked in violation of a provision of this article and instructing such owner or operator to report at the office of the chief of police, in regard to such violation. Each such owner or operator may, within 24 hours of the time such notice was attached to such vehicle, pay to the municipal court, as a penalty for and in full satisfaction of such violation, the sum of $1.00. The failure of such owner or operator to make such payment to the municipal court, within 24 hours, shall render such owner or operator subject to the penalties provided in section 1-8. (Code 1962, § 23-98; Code 1986, § 20-64) 
Sec. 86-118. - Successive violations, separate offenses.     When any vehicle shall remain parked for one hour beyond the time of the original notice of violation attached to the vehicle, such person shall be guilty of a violation of this article. Each such violation shall be punishable in accordance with section 1-8. It is the intention of this section that each hour that any vehicle shall be parked without complying with the provisions of this article shall be a separate offense and that time is the gravamen of the offense insofar as the successive violations shall occur. (Code 1962, § 23-97; Code 1986, § 20-65) 
Sec. 86-119. - Parking prohibited at certain times; illegal parking. (a)  No person employed by or operating a business or profession in that part of the city in the downtown area which is hereinafter more particularly designated shall park a privately owned or company-owned motor vehicle on any public right-of-way, whether it be an alley or a street, for the purpose of using such parking space while the owner or operator performs his duties at his regular place of employment in such downtown area. The provisions of this section shall be effective between 10:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m., Monday through Saturday of each week. (b)  Notwithstanding the provisions of subsection (a) of this section, and notwithstanding the provisions of section 86-116, a disabled person who has a handicap parking permit, who is employed by or who operates a business or profession in that part of the city in the downtown area which is hereinafter more particularly designated, shall be authorized to park in a designated disabled parking space in said downtown area at any time. The location of such parking space shall be designated by the city police with appropriate signage and markings. (c)  The parking area of the downtown area of the city wherein such parking by employees or operators of businesses or professions during said time periods shall be prohibited shall be as follows: (1)  Along the northerly and southerly sides of West Lamar Street, from its intersection with South Hampton Street and North Hampton Street to its intersection with South Lee Street and North Lee Street. (2)  Along the southerly side of East Lamar Street, from its intersection with South Lee Street to its intersection with South Price Street. (3)  Along the northerly and southerly sides of West Forsyth Street, from its intersection with North Hampton Street to its intersection with North Lee Street. (4)  Along the easterly and westerly sides of South Jackson Street, from its intersection with Church Street to its intersection with West Lamar Street. (5)  Along the easterly and westerly sides of North Jackson Street, from its intersection with West Lamar Street to its intersection with West Jefferson Street. (6)  Along the westerly side of Cotton Avenue, from its intersection with West Lamar Street to its intersection with West Forsyth Street. (7)  Along the easterly and westerly sides of Cotton Avenue, from its intersection with West Forsyth Street to its intersection with West Jefferson Street. (8)  Along the westerly side of Windsor Avenue, from its intersection with West Lamar Street to its intersection with West Forsyth Street. (9)  Along the westerly side of North Lee Street, from its intersection with West Forsyth Street to its intersection with West Jefferson Street. (d)  Upon conviction, a plea of guilty or plea of nolo contendere to a violation of the provisions of this section, the violator shall pay a fine of not less than $35.00 in addition to any other punishment or penalty which may be lawfully imposed by the municipal court of the city. (e)  The provisions of this section shall apply to the parking of motor vehicles by persons residing in upper floor residential areas as authorized by chapter 94. (Code 1986, § 20-66; Ord. No. O-87-06-12, §§ A—C, 6-22-1987; Ord. No. O-89-10-29, 10-23-1989; Ord. No. O-89-12-43, 12-18-1989; Ord. No. O-97-08-31A, 8-21-1997)

Sec. 86-121. - Parking zones on Windsor Avenue.     There is hereby established along Windsor Avenue, from its intersection with Forsyth Street to its intersection with Lamar Street, a restricted parking zone such that there shall be no parking by any person along Windsor Avenue between 10:00 a.m. and 2:00 p.m. Monday through Friday of each week. Parking along said Windsor Avenue at times other than set out above shall not be restricted except as otherwise provided in this Code. (Code 1986, § 20-68; Ord. No. O-90-06-16, 6-28-1990) 
Sec. 86-122. - Fifteen-minute parking zones.     There is hereby established a 15-minute parking zone for the two parking spaces on the north side of West Lamar Street, immediately in front of the Windsor Hotel property, and it shall be unlawful for any person to park any type of vehicle for a period longer than 15 minutes in either or both of said parking spaces. (Code 1986, § 20-69; Ord. No. O-91-10-35, 10-28-1991) 
Secs. 86-123—86-142. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LOADING ZONES 
Sec. 86-143. - Authority of police chief.     The police chief shall be authorized to designate, establish and maintain, by appropriate markings, loading zones for the purpose of loading and unloading commercial vehicles in the downtown area of the city; provided that there shall be no more than one loading zone per city block, that such loading zones shall be clearly delineated by appropriate markings and signs, and that such loading zones shall be located in such positions as will not interfere with the normal traffic flow. (Code 1986, § 20-91; Ord. No. O-88-03-13, 3-28-1988; Ord. No. O-92-03-15, 3-23-1992) 
Sec. 86-144. - Parking prohibited; exceptions.     It shall be unlawful to park any vehicle in a loading zone as designated by authority of the police chief, unless such vehicle is a commercial vehicle from which property or merchandise is being loaded or unloaded, and in no event shall such commercial vehicle park in said loading zone for a period of time longer than 30 minutes. For purposes of this article, the term "commercial vehicle" shall be defined as an automobile, truck, trailer, tractor, wagon or any other motor vehicle designed or used as a vehicle of conveyance in the furtherance of or as a part of any commercial activity or enterprise, whether or not such vehicle is used solely in such commercial activity or enterprise or is used only intermittently in such commercial activity or enterprise. (Code 1986, § 20-92; Ord. No. O-88-03-14, 3-28-1988; Ord. No. O-92-03-15, 3-23-1992) 
Secs. 86-145—86-171. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - ABANDONED VEHICLES 
Sec. 86-172. - Definitions.     The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:     Abandoned motor vehicle means a motor vehicle, which has been parked or left standing on the public streets of the city for more than five days in a nonoperating state of repair.     Abandonment means the act of the owner leaving the vehicle on the streets or sidewalks of the city for a period in excess of five days, when the owner of the vehicle does not own the property abutting the street or sidewalk upon which the vehicle is parked and does not reside, room, have a place of business, lease, rent, or otherwise exercise control and dominion over the abutting real estate.     Hazard to normal flow of traffic means a vehicle parked on the public streets of the city in a nonoperational condition and is hereby defined to be a hazard to the normal flow of traffic on the streets of the city.     Nonoperational vehicle means a vehicle that will not start, run and move under its own power in its existing condition.     Vehicle means any automobile, truck, trailer, motorcycle, wagon, or other artificial contrivance used, or capable of being used, as a means of transportation on land. (Code 1962, § 23-106; Code 1986, § 20-70) State Law reference— Similar definitions, O.C.G.A. § 40-11-1. 
Sec. 86-173. - Unlawful to abandon vehicle.     It shall be unlawful to abandon any vehicle upon the streets or sidewalks of the city. (Code 1962, §§ 23-107, 23-108; Code 1986, § 20-71) 
Sec. 86-174. - Maximum parking time.     No vehicle shall be parked upon the streets for a period of more than 24 hours unless such vehicle is owned by or in the custody, care and control of the property owner abutting said street or sidewalk where such vehicle is parked. (Code 1962, § 23-109; Code 1986, § 20-72)
