Sec. 86-175. - Abandoned vehicle to be moved within 24 hours following receipt of notice.     All such abandoned or overparked vehicles shall be moved by the owner or person in charge thereof within 24 hours following receipt of notice from the police chief or designee or any member of the police force of the city requiring such vehicle to be removed. (Code 1962, § 23-109.1; Code 1986, § 20-73) 
Sec. 86-176. - Removal of abandoned vehicle or vehicle constituting a hazard authorized.     Any vehicle which shall be abandoned, or parked so as to constitute a traffic hazard, on the streets of the city may be taken into the custody of the police department and towed or removed to a garage or parking lot either by the police chief or designee. (Code 1962, §§ 23-110, 23-112; Code 1986, § 20-74) State Law reference— When police officers may remove vehicles, O.C.G.A. §§ 40-6-206, 40-11-3. 
Sec. 86-177. - Impounding parked vehicles, removal of, authorized.     Any vehicle parked on the streets of the city in such a manner that it is a traffic hazard may be moved by the police department or towed under the custody and control and the charge for towing made and collected as herein provided. (Code 1962, § 23-112; Code 1986, § 20-75) 
Secs. 86-178—86-207. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - WEIGHT AND LOAD LIMITS[3] Footnotes: --- (3) --- State Law reference— Weight limits, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-20 et seq. 
Sec. 86-208. - Motor trucks or trailers prohibited from traversing certain areas during designated hours.     It shall be unlawful for any motor truck or motor-drawn trailer to traverse any street or part of the area of the city during periods hereafter specifically designated by the city council by resolution or ordinance. Whenever said streets or areas are designated, nothing in this section shall prevent any truck, when not accompanied by a trailer, from traversing any of the streets or areas solely for the purpose of making delivery or for the purpose of picking up or receiving goods, wares or merchandise for transportation; but this shall not include permission for trailers to enter, park or stand in such areas for any purpose whatsoever. (Code 1962, § 23-6; Code 1986, § 20-15) 
Sec. 86-209. - Limitations as to weight of vehicles on city streets. (a)  The governing body of the city shall have the right to proclaim by ordinance or resolution the maximum weight of any vehicle, including tractors and trailers, which may be driven upon certain designated streets of the city. (b)  There are hereby established certain truck routes in the city. Those trucks shall be located upon the following streets: Brady Road Carter Street Cotton Avenue East Furlow Street to Elm Avenue East Lester Street from McGarrah to Davis Elm Avenue Felder Street Forrest Street Glessner Street Industrial Boulevard Industrial Drive Jefferson Street (downtown) Lee Street to Carter Street Mathews Drive Mayo Street McGarrah Street North Dudley Street North Hampton (from Lamar north) North Jackson to Prince Street (but not between Lamar and Forsyth) Oak Avenue (from West Glessner north) Patterson Street from McGarrah to Davis Perimeter Road-Georgia Southwestern State University Prince Street Railroad Street Reese Street Simmons Street Southerfield Road Spring Street Swett Avenue Tripp Street Warren Avenue West Church Street (c)  No truck, including tractor-trailer trucks, or other motor vehicles, which weigh over 36,000 pounds gross weight, shall travel any public street within the city except for those streets listed above, unless it is necessary for such truck, tractor-trailer, or other motor vehicle to pick up or deliver a cargo on streets other than those listed above. (d)  The city shall post appropriate signs along the streets designated as truck routes. Any street not posted as a truck route shall not be considered a truck route for purposes of this section. (Code 1962, § 23-8; Code 1986, § 20-16; Ord. No. O-91-06-18, 6-20-1991; Ord. No. O-91-08-25, 8-26-1991; Ord. No. O-91-10-34, 10-28-1991; Ord. No. O-92-03-12, 3-23-1992; Ord. No. O-06-07-22, 7-20-2006; Ord. No. O-07-07-21, § 20-16, 7-19-2007; Ord. No. O-10-05-16, 5-20-2010; Ord. No. O-10-08-25, 8-19-2010) 
Sec. 86-210. - Use of engine brakes and compression brakes prohibited. (a)  For purposes of this section the terms "engine brake" or "compression brake" shall mean a device used primarily on trucks for the conversion of the engine from an internal combustion engine to an air compressor for the purpose of braking without the use of wheeled brakes, said devices being commonly referred to as "air brakes", "Jacob's brakes" or "jake brakes". (b)  It shall be unlawful for any person in actual physical control of a motor vehicle, including, but not limited to; a truck or a tractor-trailer truck, to use an engine brake or compression brake while traveling along the streets of the city unless such engine brake or compression brake is used solely to effect an emergency stop of the motor vehicle. (c)  Upon conviction, the penalty for a violation of this section shall be as provided in section 1-8 of this Code. (Ord. No. O-07-07-20, § 20-16.1, 7-19-2007) 
Chapter 90 - UTILITIES 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
Sec. 90-1. - Discontinuance of city services when charges remain unpaid.     Any person failing for any reason or refusing to pay timely the monthly water, gas, sewerage or refuse collection charges provided in this Code set by the city after having been duly billed for same by the city shall be deemed guilty of a violation of this chapter, and all water service, gas service, sewerage service and refuse collection service provided by the city to the premises for which the monthly charges are past due shall be terminated by the city; provided, however, should not more than one of the monthly water charges, gas charges, sewerage charges and refuse collection charges remain unpaid, any person may make application to the finance director to have the city services restored that are not in arrears provided such person submits a monthly repayment plan to the finance director to pay for the particular services that are in arrears within a three-month period of time from the date of such application; and provided that the person abides by each proposed monthly payment within said three-month time period. (Code 1962, § 10-22; Code 1986, § 13-1; Ord. No. O-04-12-33, 12-16-2004) 
Sec. 90-2. - Refunds of utility payments. (a)  In the event that a city utility customer claims that he has overpaid a utility bill or that he has been charged more than was legally due for the use of city utilities, then such customer may file a claim for a refund with the finance director at any time within three years after the date of the payment of the amount for which a refund is claimed. The claim for refund shall be in writing, and shall be in a form and contain the information required by the finance director. Such claim shall include a summary statement of the grounds upon which the customer relies in claiming the refund. The customer may be required to provide such additional information as may be requested by the finance director in order for the clerk to consider the claim. (b)  Upon receipt of the claim, and any additional information required from the customer by the finance director, the finance director shall consider the claim and determine whether or not the customer is entitled to a refund, but in no event shall any refund be provided for any payments made more than three years prior to the date of filing the claim for refund. The finance director shall only grant the claim for refund if the finance director determines that the amount for which the refund is sought was billed to the customer erroneously or illegally. (c)  The finance director shall notify the customer of the finance director's decision regarding the refund claim within 30 days from the date that the finance director receives all information necessary in order for the finance director to make a determination regarding the refund claim. (d)  Any customer whose claim for refund is denied by the finance director may appeal such denial to the city council within 30 days of the date of the finance director's decision. The city council shall authorize such refund only in the event that it finds that the funds for which the refund is sought were billed to the customer either erroneously or illegally. The decision of the city council regarding the claim for refund shall be final. (Code 1986, § 13-2; Ord. No. O-97-11-36, 11-20-1997; Ord. No. O-04-12-33, 12-16-2004) 
Secs. 90-3—90-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - BACKFLOW CONTROL[1] Footnotes: --- (1) --- Editor's note— Ord. No. O-11-11-25, exh. A, adopted Nov. 17, 2011, amended art. II in its entirety to read as herein set out, with the exception of § 90-32, which remains unchanged. Former art. II, §§ 90-23—90-32, pertained to similar subject matter and derived from: Code 1986, §§ 13-40—13-48; Ord. No. O-85-07-16, §§ 1—3, adopted June 27, 1985; and Ord. No. O-95-11-35, adopted Nov. 30, 1995. 
Sec. 90-23. - Definitions.     The definitions found in the city plumbing code for backflow, cross-connections, and backflow prevention devices shall be those used in this article. In addition, the following definitions shall apply:     Air gap means a physical separation sufficient to prevent backflow between the free-flowing discharge end of the potable water system and any other system. Physically defined as a distance equal to twice the diameter of the supply side pipe diameter but never less than one inch.     Approved means accepted by the director of public works as meeting an applicable specification stated or cited in this regulation, or as suitable for the proposed use.     Auxiliary water supply means any water supply on or available to the premises other than the city's approved public water supply. These auxiliary waters may include water from another purveyor's public potable water supply or any natural sources such as a well, spring, river, stream, harbor, etc., or used waters or industrial fluids. These waters may be contaminated or polluted or they may be objectionable and constitute an unacceptable water source over which the city does not have sanitary control.     Backflow means the flow of water or other liquids, mixtures, or substances under positive or reduced pressure in the distribution pipes of a potable water supply from any source other than its intended source.     Backflow preventer means a device or means designed to prevent backflow or backsiphonage. Most commonly categorized as air gap, reduced pressure principal assembly, double-check valve assembly, pressure vacuum breaker, atmospheric vacuum breaker, hose bibb vacuum breaker, residential dual check and barometric loop.     Containment means a method of backflow prevention which requires a backflow preventer at the water service entrance.     Contaminant means a substance that will impair the quality of the water to a degree that it creates a serious health hazard to the public, leading to poisoning or the spread of disease.     Contamination means an impairment of the quality of the potable water by sewage, industrial fluids or waste liquids, compounds or other materials to a degree which creates an actual or potential hazard to the public health through poisoning or through the spread of disease.     Cross-connection means a connection or potential connection between any part of a potable water system and any other environment containing other substances in a manner that, under any circumstances, would allow such substances to enter the potable water system. Other substances may be gases, liquids or solids, such as chemicals, waste products, steam, water from other sources (potable or nonpotable), or any other matter that may change the color and/or add odor to the water.     Cross-connection control by containment means the installation of an approved backflow prevention device at the water service connection to any customer's premises where it is physically and economically infeasible to find and permanently eliminate or control all actual or potential cross-connections within the customer's water system; or, it shall mean the installation of an approved backflow prevention device on the service line leading to and supplying a portion of a customer's water system where there are actual or potential cross-connections which cannot be effectively eliminated or controlled at the point of the cross-connection.     Cross-connection, controlled means a connection between a potable water system and a nonpotable water system with an approved backflow prevention device properly installed and maintained so that it will continuously afford the protection commensurate with the degree of hazard.     Customer means a person or entity receiving water or sewer services from the City of Americus Public Works Department.     Department means the City of Americus Public Works Department.     Double-check backflow preventer means an assembly of two independently operating spring-loaded check valves with tightly-closing shut off valves on each side of the check valves and properly located test cocks allowing for the testing of each check valve on each line, specifically a double-check valve assembly (DCVA) or a double-check detector assembly (DCDA).     Hazard assessment means a hazard determination conducted pursuant to Section 608 of the Georgia State Minimum Standard Plumbing Code.     Hazard, degree of, means the term is derived from an evaluation of the potential risk to public health and the adverse effect of the hazard upon the potable water system.     Hazard, health, means any condition, device, or practice in the water supply system and its operation which could create, or in the judgment of the building official, may create a danger to the health and well-being of the water consumer.     Hazard, plumbing, means a plumbing-type cross-connection in a consumer's potable water system that has not been properly protected by an approved air gap or approved backflow prevention device.     Hazard, pollutional, means an actual or potential threat to the physical properties of the water system or to the potability of the public or the consumer's potable water system but which would constitute a nuisance or be aesthetically objectionable or could cause damage to the system or its appurtenances, but would not be dangerous to health.     Hazard, system, means an actual or potential threat of severe damage to the physical properties of the public potable water system or the consumer's potable water system or of a pollution or contamination which would have a protracted effect on the quality of the potable water in the system.     Industrial fluids system means any system containing a fluid or solution which may be chemically, biologically or otherwise contaminated or polluted in a form or concentration such as would constitute a health, system, pollutional or plumbing hazard if introduced into an approved water supply. This may include, but is not limited to: Polluted or contaminated waters; all types of process waters and used waters originating from the public potable water system which may have deteriorated in sanitary quality; chemicals in fluid form; plating acids and alkalies; circulating cooling water connected to an open cooling tower and/or cooling towers that are chemically or biologically treated or stabilized with toxic substances; contaminated natural waters such as from wells, springs, streams, rivers, bays, harbors, seas, irrigation canals or systems, etc.; oils, gases, glycerine, paraffins, caustic and acid solutions and other liquid and gaseous fluids used in industrial or other purposes or for firefighting purposes.     Owner means any person who has legal title to, or license to operate or inhabit, a property upon which a cross-connection inspection is to be made or upon which a cross-connection is deemed likely by the City of Americus Public Works.     Permit means a document issued by the department which allows the installation of a backflow preventer.     Person means any individual, partnership, company, public or private corporation, political subdivision or agency of the state department, agency or instrumentality or the United States or any other legal entity.     Pollutant means a foreign substance that, if permitted to get into the public water system, will degrade its quality so as to constitute a moderate hazard or impair the usefulness or quality of the water to a degree that does not create an actual hazard to the public health, but which does adversely and unreasonably affect such water for domestic use.     Reduced pressure principle backflow preventer means an assembly consisting of two independently operating approved check valves with an automatically operating differential relief valve located between the two check valves, tightly-closing shut-off valves on each side of the check valves and properly located test cocks allowing for the testing of the check valves and the relief valve on each line, specifically a reduced pressure principal assembly (RP) or a reduced pressure principal detector assembly (RPDA).     Residential dual check means an assembly of two spring loaded, independently operating check valves without tightly closing shut-off valves or test cocks. Generally employed immediately downstream of the water meter to act as a containment device.     Water service connection means the terminal end of a service connection from the public potable water system, i.e., where the water purveyor loses jurisdiction and sanitary control over the water at its point of delivery to the customer's water system. If a meter is installed at the end of the service connection, then the term "service connection" shall mean the downstream end of the meter. There shall be no unprotected takeoffs from the service line ahead of any meter or backflow prevention device located at the point of delivery to the customer's water system. Service connection shall also include water service connection from a fire hydrant and all other temporary or emergency water service connections from the public potable water system.     Water used means any water supplied by the city from the public potable water system to a consumer's water system after it has passed through the point of delivery and is no longer under the sanitary control of the city water department. (Ord. No. O-11-11-25, exh. A, 11-17-2011) 
Sec. 90-24. - Purpose.     The purpose of this article is to: (1)  Protect the public potable water supply of the city from the possibility of contamination or pollution by containing within the customer's internal distribution systems or the customer's private water systems such contaminates or pollutants which could backflow into the public water system through an undiscovered or uncontrolled cross-connection on said premises; (2)  Promote the elimination or control of existing cross-connections, actual or potential, between the customer's in-plant potable water systems and nonpotable water systems, plumbing fixtures and industrial piping systems; and (3)  Provide for the maintenance of a continuing program of cross-connection control which will systematically attempt to prevent the contamination or pollution of all potable water systems. (Ord. No. O-11-11-25, exh. A, 11-17-2011) 
Sec. 90-25. - Protection of system; fees and charges; installation of assemblies. (a)  In accordance with the Federal Safe Drinking Water Act of 1974, and the Georgia Rules for Safe Drinking Water Section 391-3-5-.13, the Water Purveyor, City of Americus Public Works, has the primary responsibility for preventing water from unapproved sources, or any other substances, from entering the public potable water system. (b)  The City of Americus is authorized to charge a nominal fee to water customers for the purpose of funding the cross-connection control program. The City of Americus is also authorized to charge an additional fee to businesses for funding the cross-connection control program and the associated inspections. Should a water customer fail to comply with the requirements set out herein, the City of Americus has the authority to install, test, and repair backflow prevention assemblies and pass on costs to the customer associated with the work, including, but not limited to, labor, parts and administration. The City of Americus Public Works Department has the authority to hire or designate an on-call or consulting engineer to offer support with tasks associated with upkeep of the cross-connection control program. (Ord. No. O-11-11-25, exh. A, 11-17-2011) 
Sec. 90-25.1. - Obligations and responsibilities.     The following obligations shall be undertaken and performed by the named persons or entities: (1)  Purveyor. The Director of Public Works for the City of Americus, Georgia, or a designee on his or her behalf, as authorized through this article, is primarily responsible for preventing contamination and pollution of the public water supply by instituting the cross-connection control program, as approved by the Georgia Environmental Protection Division. Such responsibility begins at the point of origin for the public potable water supply, includes all of the distribution system, and terminates at the service connection for the customer's water system. In addition, the director shall exercise reasonable vigilance to ensure that the customer adheres to this policy and these procedures as stated and outlined herein. (2)  Customer. The business and residential customers will be responsible for all work and costs related to installing, certifying and maintaining the required backflow assemblies. The required customer-supplied backflow prevention assembly at the service connection shall provide maximum protection for locations deemed "high hazard" (reduced pressure principal backflow preventer — RP, RPDA or air gap), or minimum protection for locations deemed "low hazard" (double-check backflow preventer — DCVA, DCDA) as directed by the department or an authorized representative thereof. (3)  Building code official. The building inspection department is primarily responsible for enforcing the State of Georgia Plumbing Code to prevent contamination and pollution within the customer's water system in accordance with applicable plumbing and building codes requiring that all outlets terminate through an approved air gap or be controlled by an approved mechanical backflow prevention device. Such responsibility begins at the service connection to the premises and extends to the extremities of the customer's potable water supply. (Ord. No. O-11-11-25, exh. A, 11-17-2011; Ord. No. O-12-04-09, 4-19-2012) 
Sec. 90-26. - Water system components.     The water system shall be considered as made up of two parts: The utility system and the customer system. (1)  Utility system. The utility system shall consist of the source facilities and the distribution system and shall include all those facilities of the water system under the complete control of the city, up to the point where the customer's system begins. a.  Source facilities. The source shall include all components of the facilities utilized in the production, treatment, storage and delivery of water to the distribution system. b.  Distribution system. The distribution system shall include the network of conduits used for the delivery of water from the source to the customer's system. (2)  Customer's system. The customer's system shall include those parts of the facilities beyond the termination of the utility distribution system which are utilized in conveying utility-delivered domestic water to points of use. (Ord. No. O-11-11-25, exh. A, 11-17-2011) 
Sec. 90-27. - Connection policy. (a)  No water service connection to any premises shall be installed or maintained by the city unless the water supply is protected as required by state law and regulations and this article. The City of Americus shall either discontinue service of water to any premises or take appropriate steps by installing, testing or maintaining a backflow prevention assembly if one is required by this article and state law and has not been tested and maintained, or if it is found that a required backflow prevention assembly has been removed or bypassed, or if an unprotected cross-connection exists on the premises. In the event of disconnection, service will not be restored until such conditions or defects are corrected. Compliance with applicable requirements for backflow prevention shall be verified by the department before water service is reinstated. (b)  The customer's system shall be open for inspection at all reasonable times to the department or authorized representatives of the department to determine whether cross-connections or other structural or sanitary hazards, including violations of these regulations, exist. When such a condition becomes known, the department shall either immediately discontinue service to the premises by providing for a physical break in the service line until the customer has corrected the conditions in conformance with state statutes and city ordinances relating to plumbing and water supplies, and the regulations adopted pursuant thereto, or take appropriate steps by installing, testing or maintaining the assembly to correct the conditions in conformance with state statutes and city ordinances relating to plumbing and water supplies, and the regulations adopted pursuant thereto. All costs incurred shall be passed directly to the customer. (Ord. No. O-11-11-25, exh. A, 11-17-2011) 
Sec. 90-28. - Installation of assembly in service line.     An approved backflow prevention assembly shall also be installed on each service line to a customer's water system at or near the property line or immediately inside the building being served; but, in all cases, before the first branch line leading off the service line wherever the following conditions exist: (1)  Auxiliary water supply. In the case of premises having an auxiliary water supply which is not or may not be of safe bacteriological or chemical quality and which is not acceptable as an additional source by the building official, the public water system shall be protected against backflow from the premises by eliminating the connection between the two systems. (2)  Industrial fluid or hazardous substances. In the case of premises on which any industrial fluid or any other objectionable substance is handled in such a fashion as to create an actual or potential hazard to the public water system, the public system shall be protected against backflow from the premises by installing an approved backflow prevention assembly in the service line appropriate to the degree of hazard. This shall include the handling of process waters and waters originating from the utility system which have been subject to deterioration in quality. (3)  Connection issues. In the case of premises having: a.  Internal cross-connections that cannot be permanently corrected and controlled; b.  Intricate plumbing and piping arrangements; or c.  Where entry to all portions of the premises is not readily accessible for inspection purposes, making it impracticable or impossible to ascertain whether or not dangerous cross-connections exist. The public water system shall be protected against backflow from the premises by installing an approved backflow prevention assembly in the service line. (4)  Water heating or pressure producing device. In the case of premises having any water heating device or any other pressure-producing device connected to the customer's system, a thermal protection device, either a thermal expansion tank or a calibrated pressure-relief valve set at 80 psi, will be required in order to protect against damage caused by thermal expansion of a system closed with backflow preventer. (Ord. No. O-11-11-25, exh. A, 11-17-2011) 
Sec. 90-29. - Type of assembly.     The type of protective assembly required under subsections 90-28(1)—(3) shall depend upon the degree of hazard which exists as follows: (1)  Auxiliary water supply. In the case of any premises where there is an auxiliary water supply as stated in subsection 90-28(1) and it is not subject to any of the following rules, the public water system shall be protected by an approved air gap separation or an approved reduced pressure principle backflow prevention assembly. (2)  Objectionable substances. In the case of any premises where there is water or substance that would be objectionable, but not hazardous to health, if introducted into the public water system, the public water system shall be protected by an approved double-check valve assembly. (3)  Hazardous substances. In the case of any premises where there is any material dangerous to health which is handled in such a fashion as to create an actual or potential hazard to the public water system, the public water system shall be protected by an approved air gap separation or any approved reduced pressure principle backflow prevention assembly. Examples of premises where these conditions will exist include sewage treatment plants, sewage pumping stations, chemical manufacturing plants, hospitals, mortuaries and plating plants. (4)  Connection issues. In the case of any premises where there are uncontrolled cross-connections, either actual or potential, the public water system shall be protected by an approved air gap separation or an approved reduced pressure principle backflow prevention assembly at the service connection. (5)  Other prohibitions or restrictions. In the case of any premises where, because of security requirements or other prohibitions or restrictions, it is impossible or impractical to make a complete in-plant cross-connection survey, the public water system shall be protected against backflow from the premises by either an approved air gap separation or an approved reduced pressure principle backflow prevention assembly on each service to the premises. (6)  Unknown hazards. In the case of any premises where there is no known pollutional or contaminant hazard, as described or covered in subsections (1) through (5) of this section, the public water system shall be protected by an approved residential dual-check valve at the service connection. (Ord. No. O-11-11-25, exh. A, 11-17-2011) 
Sec. 90-30. - Approved backflow prevention assembly.     Any backflow prevention assembly device assembly required herein shall be a model and size approved by the building official. The term "approved backflow prevention assembly" shall mean an assembly that has been manufactured in full conformance with the standards established in the city and state plumbing codes. (Ord. No. O-11-11-25, exh. A, 11-17-2011) 
Sec. 90-31. - Tests; repair of assemblies. (a)  Periodic testing. Annual testing shall be performed by a tester certified by one of the approved programs. This testing will be coordinated by the owner and performed at the owner's expense. Assemblies shall also be tested immediately following installation, repair or relocation of an assembly. Test reports must be submitted within seven days from the date that the test is performed. Any backflow preventer that fails during a periodic test will be repaired or replaced. When repairs are necessary, upon completion of the repair, the assembly will be retested at the customer's expense to insure correct operation. In situations where the public water system is not deemed by the department to be immediately threatened by a health or pollutional hazard, a compliance date of not more than 30 days after the test date will be established. If a customer does not comply with installation, testing or repair within 60 days of notifications, the department may perform installation, testing or repair and bill the customer for the cost of the work, parts, and any associated administrative costs. (b)  Backflow assembly testers. In accordance with the State of Georgia Environmental Protection Division requirements, backflow testers for the City of Americus must be certified by one of the State of Georgia approved agencies in order to test backflow assemblies. Certification is valid for up to three years or until such time as his or her certification expires, whichever comes first. In order to certify backflow prevention assemblies for the City of Americus, testers must complete an application, including, but not limited to, a copy of his or her current tester certificate from one of the approved agencies, a copy of the current calibration certificate of the approved backflow gauge to be used by the tester, and the business license under which he or she will be practicing. A list of testers will be published and made available to customers who require a backflow assembly test. (c)  Backflow assembly repairs. All backflow assembly repairs shall be performed by a person or persons working under a current plumber's license. (d)  Backflow assembly installation. In accordance with State of Georgia's Cross-Connection Control requirements, all installations of backflow assemblies shall be performed by a person or persons working under a current plumber's license. (Ord. No. O-11-11-25, exh. A, 11-17-2011) 
Sec. 90-31.1. - Installation of residential dual-checks.     Residential dual-checks shall be installed by the department or a designee thereof. (Ord. No. O-11-11-25, exh. A, 11-17-2011) 
Sec. 90-32. - Nonconforming devices.     All presently installed backflow prevention devices which do not meet the requirements of this section, but were approved devices for the purposes described herein at the time of installation and which have been properly maintained, shall, except for the inspection and maintenance requirements under section 90-31, be excluded from the requirements of these rules so long as the building official is assured that they will satisfactorily protect the utility system. Whenever the existing device is moved from the present location or requires more than minimum maintenance or when the building official finds that the maintenance constitutes a hazard to health, the unit shall be replaced by an approved backflow prevention device meeting the requirements of this section. (Code 1986, § 13-49; Ord. No. O-85-07-16, § 3.2.7, 6-27-1985; Ord. No. O-95-11-35, 11-30-1995) 
Secs. 90-33—90-52. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - WATER AND SEWER LINE EXTENSIONS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
Secs. 90-53—90-77. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - COMMERCIAL AREAS 
Sec. 90-78. - Authority to extend; service charges. (a)  The city council shall be authorized to extend or cause to be extended water main lines and sewer main lines into commercial areas, both inside and outside the city limits where the city council deems it appropriate and in the best interest of the city to do so. (b)  In considering the extension of such water mains and sewer mains, the city council shall take into consideration past commercial business growth patterns and anticipated commercial business growth patterns, both inside and outside the city limits. The city council shall also weigh the net cost to the city of such extensions against the potential increased revenues to the city realized or anticipated to result from such extensions due to increased economic development activity. (c)  In the event that the city council determines that it is appropriate to extend water mains and sewer mains into commercial areas, either inside or outside the city limits, the city shall be authorized to charge to new water and sewer customers, in addition to tap charges, service deposits, meter costs and monthly water and sewer rates, an amount determined by the city which will reimburse the city for all reasonable costs of extending such water mains and sewer mains based upon the linear front footage of the property to be served by such water main and sewer main extensions. Such costs need not be paid by a property owner or owners until such time as the property owner or owners desire to purchase city water and city sewer services, and such charges may be paid as part of the initial tap charges otherwise authorized in this Code. In addition to the foregoing, the city shall be authorized to charge interest on such amounts from the date that such water and sewer service becomes available to the date that such charges are paid in an amount to be determined by the city. (d)  The charges authorized hereunder shall be in addition to all other charges authorized to persons or businesses who utilize city water and city sewer services, whether inside or outside the city limits. (e)  The commercial business shall be required to pay the full cost of installing water and sewer lines from the main line to a commercial business building or buildings located on the premises, and the city shall have no responsibility or liability therefor. (f)  The provisions of this section shall not apply to residential subdivisions, or to the extension of water mains and sewer mains by the city to serve a single residence or a single commercial business. Under such circumstances, the city shall be authorized to undertake such extensions and shall be authorized to charge the full cost of such extensions to such residential or commercial customer. (Code 1986, § 13-150; Ord. No. O-96-04-15, 4-18-1996) 
Secs. 90-79—90-99. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - RESIDENTIAL AREAS 
Sec. 90-100. - Authority to extend.     The city council shall be authorized to extend or cause to be extended water main lines and sewer main lines into residential areas, both inside and outside the city limits, where the city council deems it appropriate and in the best interest of the city to do so. For purposes of this division, the term "residential areas" shall include all areas inside and outside the city limits which are zoned for any type of residential development. (Code 1986, § 13-161; Ord. No. O-99-01-03, § 1, 1-21-1999) 
Sec. 90-101. - Investigation; survey; estimated costs. (a)  In the event that the utilities director shall determine that there is an area within the city or outside the city limits which should have access to city water and city sewerage, the utilities director shall conduct a preliminary investigation of the area to determine the estimated cost, feasibility, and if appropriate, the time frame within which water mains and sewer mains could be installed to serve such area. The utilities director shall then make a written report of his findings to the city manager of the city, who shall review such findings and submit them to the city council for review. (b)  Upon review of the findings, the city council shall be authorized to undertake one of the following three options: (1)  The council can determine that the proposed installation of water and sewer lines in such area is not feasible, not cost effective, or is a project that the city should not undertake at the present time. (2)  In the event that the area studied is an area where residential property has already been developed, then the city council shall be authorized to direct the city manager of the city to undertake a survey of the property owners in the area to determine whether or not they desire the construction of such improvements in the area. An estimated cost of such extension that would have to be paid by such property owners, if any, shall be submitted to said property owners as part of such survey. Unless the city council shall determine that public health and safety concerns exist so as to require such installation, in the discretion of the city council, no such extension shall be undertaken by the city unless at least 60 percent of the property owners in the subject area respond affirmatively to such survey. (3)  In the event that the subject area has not been developed as a residential area, then the city council shall direct the city manager to conduct a survey, as referred to in subsection (b)(2) of this section, of the property owners in the subject area in the same manner. Unless the city council shall determine that public health and safety concerns exist so as to require such installation, in the discretion of the city council, no such extension shall be undertaken by the city unless 100 percent of the property owners in the subject area respond affirmatively to such survey. (Code 1986, § 13-162; Ord. No. O-99-01-03, § 2, 1-21-1999; Ord. No. O-2015-15, 7-23-2015) 
Sec. 90-102. - Completion of survey; determination of special or general benefits. (a)  The survey shall be completed within 90 days after the city manager is directed to commence such survey. In the event that the required percentage approval from the property owners is met as a result of the survey, or in the event that the city council determines that public health and safety concerns exist so as to require the installation of the water and sewer improvements, the city council shall determine whether or not a special benefit will accrue to those property owners gaining access to the city's water and sewer system. In the event that such a special benefit will accrue as determined by the city council, the city council shall compare such special benefit with the general benefit derived by taxpayers of the city in general as a result of such improvements. If the comparison of the special benefit to the general benefit derived by taxpayers of the city in general results in a conclusion that the special benefit to the taxpayers of the subject area in expanding the water and sewer system to said area will outweigh the general benefit derived by taxpayers of the city in general, then in such event, the city council shall determine what portion of the cost of extending the city's water and sewer line to the subject area will be paid by the city, if any. If the city council determines that the general benefit to be derived by taxpayers of the city in general outweighs the special benefit to the property owners in the subject area, then the city shall pay the total cost of the extension of the water and sewer line. (b)  In the event that the city determines there is a special benefit to the property owners in the subject area, the city shall determine what portion of such cost each property owner shall pay for such water and sewer extension. If finally approved, the portion of the cost of the water and sewer line extension payable by the property owners in the subject area shall be paid to the city in accord with the provisions of this division. (Code 1986, § 13-163; Ord. No. O-99-01-03, § 3, 1-21-1999; Ord. No. O-2015-15, 7-23-2015) 
Sec. 90-103. - Boundary of subject area; total costs; assessment. (a)  At the next regular meeting of the city council after completion of the survey and the tabulations of the results thereof, or at such other time as the city council may determine. The city council may consider a resolution establishing the boundary of the subject area to be served by the water and sewer extensions and identifying all of the property or properties in the subject area which will benefit from access to such extension. Such resolution shall also provide the following: (1)  The total cost of the proposed project; (2)  The proposed method of assessment as to each property owner; (3)  A good faith estimate of the proposed assessment against each property; and (4)  A date, place, and time for a public hearing to be held on the merits of the project and on any objections thereto. (b)  Such resolution, if approved by the city council, shall be deemed to conditionally approve the project under the terms and conditions as set out in the resolution, but such project shall not proceed until after the public hearing and after the city council has approved a final resolution approving the project in accord with the terms of such final resolution. (c)  Notice of the public hearing, referred to in subsection (b) of this section, shall be given to every property owner identified in the preliminary resolution as potentially benefiting from access to the proposed water and sewer line improvements. Such notice shall be given in writing and mailed to such property owners by certified mail, return receipt requested, at the address shown on the city tax digest for the mailing of tax notices. Such notices shall be mailed at least 15 days prior to the date of the public hearing and shall include a copy of the preliminary resolution as approved by the city council. Such notice shall also specify the date, time, and location of the hearing and advise such property owners of their right to attend said hearing and to testify at said hearing. Such notice shall also be published by the city manager or his designee at least once a week for two consecutive weeks in the legal organ of the city. The time fixed for the public hearing shall be not less than five nor more than ten days after the date of the last publication of such notice. (d)  The city council shall hold the public hearing on the date, time, and place specified for the purpose of hearing supporting comments, complaints, objections that may be made by any interested persons concerning the project, including, but not limited to, the need for such water and sewer extension, the basis of apportioning costs between the city and the property owners, or the amount of the proposed assessment. The city council shall consider such comments and shall also be authorized to accept written comments from interested parties. (e)  At the next regular meeting of the city council, or at such other time as the city council may direct, the city council shall be authorized to consider a final resolution authorizing the project. Such resolution shall not be approved at the meeting at which it is first read without unanimous consent of the members of the city council, but shall be voted upon by the city council at the time of the second reading of such resolution. Such resolution shall include, but shall not be limited to, the following determinations. (1)  The boundary of the subject area to be served by the water and sewer extension; (2)  The projected cost of the improvements; (3)  The proposed method of assessment of such costs against the property owners; (4)  A good faith estimate of the proposed assessment against each property owner; and (5)  The date on which such assessments shall be due and payable to the city. (Code 1986, § 13-164; Ord. No. O-99-01-03, § 4, 1-21-1999; Ord. No. O-2015-15, 7-23-2015) 
Sec. 90-104. - Notice of assessment. (a)  The city manager of the city, or his designee, shall, not less than 30 days before the date on which the payment of an assessment shall be due, cause written notice of such assessment to be sent to each affected property owner by certified mail, return receipt requested. The notice shall inform the property owner of the amount of the assessment, that the assessment is payable to the finance director of the city, that if paid on or before the due date, such assessment shall be without interest, and that if such assessment is not paid by the due date, the amount of such assessment shall be a lien against the lot or tracts of land subject to the assessment, and such lien shall continue in force until the assessment and all interest is fully paid. The interest to be charged on assessments not paid when due shall be determined by the city council in the final resolution in section 90-103. (b)  In addition to the foregoing notice of the property owner's right to pay such assessment in installments, as provided in this division, shall also be contained in the notice required under this section. (Code 1986, § 13-165; Ord. No. O-99-01-03, § 5, 1-21-1999; Ord. No. O-04-12-33, 12-16-2004; Ord. No. O-2015-15, 7-23-2015) 
Sec. 90-105. - Action to enjoin or contest assessments.     No action shall be authorized to set aside any assessment, to enjoin the collection of any assessment, to enjoin the issuance of any execution therefor, or to contest the validity of an assessment on any legal or equitable grounds, unless such action is commenced within 30 days after the receipt of the notice provided for in section 90-104. (Code 1986, § 13-166; Ord. No. O-99-01-03, § 6, 1-21-1999) 
Sec. 90-106. - Payment of assessment by installments.     When an assessment is imposed against a property owner for the installation of water and sewer lines as set out in this division, and the property owner desires to pay the assessment in installments, the property owner shall be authorized to pay such assessment in installments if notice of such election shall be given by the property to the chief administrator officer of the city on or before the due date of the assessment, subject to the following terms: (1)  The assessment may be amortized over such length of time as requested by the property owner, but no such assessment may be amortized over more than seven years. (2)  The interest rate to be charged to a property owner shall be based upon the cost of funds to the city in connection with such project, plus administrative expenses and costs incurred by the city in administering the payments. Notwithstanding the foregoing, in the event that the water and sewer line extension project is paid for with cash funds from the city's water and sewer fund, the interest rate to be charged to property owners who amortize their assessment shall be the rate that the money expended for such extension would have earned if such money had been invested in one-year certificates of deposit, plus administrative expenses and costs incurred by the city in administering the payments. (3)  Each assessment amortized, as provided in this section, shall be repaid in equal monthly installments of principal and interest according to an amortization schedule provided by the city manager. Such assessments shall be evidenced by a promissory note and such other documents as may be deemed necessary or appropriate to evidence such indebtedness and to secure the repayment thereof. In the event that the property owner is a utility customer of the city, the city shall be authorized to add the monthly installment to the monthly utility bill of the property owner. In the event the property owner is not a utility customer of the city, a monthly installment shall be billed to the property owner by the city. (4)  The amount of the assessment shall be a lien against the property of the property owner subject to such assessment until such time as all principal and interest are fully paid. Such liens shall be levied, enforced, and collected in the same manner as provided for the collection of city taxes. (5)  In the event that any installment is not paid in full when due, the finance director of the city shall be authorized to notify the property owner that the assessment is in default and such officer shall be further authorized to declare the entire unpaid balance, with interest, costs, and expenses, immediately due and payable. (6)  Upon the sale, donation, gift, or other transfer by operation of law of any real property subject to such a lien, such assessment shall be due and payable in full at the time of such transfer; provided, however, that transfers of property solely for the purpose of securing a bona fide indebtedness of the property owner shall not require payment in full of such lien upon such transfer. (7)  Notwithstanding the other provisions of this section regarding the repayment of such assessments amortized over a period of years, in the event that the subject area has no residential dwellings located on it at the time of the approval of the final resolution approving the project as provided in this division, then, in such event, the property owners shall be authorized to enter into an agreement with the city to provide that such assessment shall be paid, with interest as aforesaid, at the time that each lot in the proposed development is sold, provided that the entire assessment, whether or not all lots subject to such assessment have been sold, shall be paid no later than seven years from the initial due date of the assessment. All other provisions of this division relating to interest rates, liens for assessments, and default shall be applicable to such property owners. (Code 1986, § 13-167; Ord. No. O-99-01-03, § 7, 1-21-1999; Ord. No. O-04-12-33, 12-16-2004; Ord. No. O-2015-15, 7-23-2015) 
Sec. 90-107. - Special fund for assessments.     All assessments levied and collected under this division shall be retained by the finance director of the city in a special fund to be used and applied for the payment of expenses incurred in installing and extending water and sewer lines for the project identified in the final resolution referred to in this division. No money in said special fund shall be used for any other purpose until such time as all costs of such project have been paid in full. In the event that any funds remain in the special fund after the project has been paid for in full, then such remaining funds shall be transferred to the city water and sewer fund. (Code 1986, § 13-168; Ord. No. O-99-01-03, § 8, 1-21-1999; Ord. No. O-04-12-33, 12-16-2004) 
Sec. 90-108. - Property required to connect and pay monthly usage cost.     Upon approval of the final resolution referred to in this division authorizing the commencement of the project in the subject area, the city shall be authorized to require that each property in the subject area which is to benefit from the extension of the water and sewer lines as a result of such project shall be required to connect to such water and sewer lines and pay the monthly usage cost as established under this chapter, in addition to the payment of such assessments as may be levied under the terms of this division. (Code 1986, § 13-169; Ord. No. O-99-01-03, § 9, 1-21-1999) 
Sec. 90-109. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - ANNEXATION OF RESIDENTIAL AND COMMERCIAL AREAS 
Sec. 90-110. - Annexation application; utility extensions.     Upon any property owner submitting an application for annexation of such property owner's property into the city under any applicable method of annexation, if the property to be annexed is not being served by city water service or city sanitary sewer service at the time of the filing of such annexation petition, and if the property to be annexed has already been developed to the extent that it already has constructed on it residential or commercial buildings, then, as a part of the annexation process, the governing body of the city shall be authorized to consider proceeding in accord with the terms of this article with respect to the extension of water mains, sewer mains, water taps, and sewer taps to the property which is the subject of the annexation in accord with the terms of this division. (Ord. No. O-2013-24, 9-19-2013) 
Sec. 90-111. - Definitions.     For the purposes of this division, the following terms shall have the following meanings:     "Annexation" means the annexation of real property into the incorporated limits of the City of Americus pursuant to any method authorized by Georgia law.     "Project" means the construction of water line extensions, sewer line extensions, installation of water tap fees, or installation of sewer tap fees, or all of the above.     "Property owner" means the person or entity which owns fee simple title to the subject property and is the annexation applicant with respect to the subject property.     "Qualified property" means subject property which is situated such that existing city water services and existing city sewer services can be lawfully extended to such property without excessive costs, without placing an undue burden upon the capacity of the utility system, and without permanently disrupting utility service to existing city utility service customers.     "Sewer line extension costs" means the cost to be incurred by the city is extending existing city sewerage line from the existing city sewerage system to a location from which the subject property could be served. Such cost shall include, but shall not be limited to, the cost of easement or right-or-way acquisition.     "Subject property" means the improved real property located outside the incorporated limits of the city which the property owner is seeking to annex into the city.     "Water line extension costs" means the cost to be incurred by the city in extending existing city water lines from the existing city water system to a location from which the subject property could be served. Such cost shall include, but shall not be limited to, the cost of easement or right-or-way acquisition. (Ord. No. O-2013-24, 9-19-2013) 
Sec. 90-112. - Initial review of application.     If the property to be annexed is "qualified property" as defined in this division, and if the property owner makes appropriate application for the extension of water and sewer services to the property to be annexed under this division, then the community development department, working in conjunction with the city utilities department and the city fire and emergency services department, shall undertake an initial review of the application. If such departments determine, as a result of such initial review, that the property to be annexed is "qualified property" under this division, then the departments shall jointly determine whether it is economically feasible from a financial standpoint for the governing body to provide the property owner, as a condition of annexation, reduced costs and fees for water line extensions, sewer line extensions, water tap fees, and sewer tap fees. No such cost or fee reductions shall be authorized unless the net cost of such project shall result in a financial benefit to the city. (Ord. No. O-2013-24, 9-19-2013) 
Sec. 90-113. - Financial benefit determination.     In determining financial benefit to the city in connection with such project, said departments shall perform a cost analysis to determine the cost of water line extensions, sewer line extensions, water tap fees, and sewer tap fees to the subject property. Such analysis shall include consideration of the following: (1)  Cost to extend water lines; (2)  Cost to extend sewer lines; (3)  Cost for project engineering; (4)  Cost of water tap fees; (5)  Cost of sewer tap fees; (6)  Cost of stormwater fees; (7)  Estimated revenue to city from ad valorem property taxes, water service fees, sewer service fees, garbage fees, and stormwater fees; and (8)  Any other information that either department deems appropriate to include in connection with such analysis. (Ord. No. O-2013-24, 9-19-2013) 
Sec. 90-114. - Recommendation to city council.     The departments shall jointly recommend to the governing body of the city the actual amount of fee reductions, if any, that would be authorized for the proposed project based upon such calculations conditioned upon the subject property being annexed into the city; provided, however, that in no event shall fee reductions exceed a seven-year payback to the city which shall be calculated solely based upon increased ad valorem tax revenue to the city generated by the subject property. (Ord. No. O-2013-24, 9-19-2013) 
Sec. 90-115. - Payment of fees in installments under certain circumstances.     With respect to any water line extension costs, sewer line extensions costs, water tap fees, or sewer tap fees which are to be paid by a property owner annexing property into the city: (i) where the subject property is not qualified property as defined in section 90-111; (ii) where all or a portion of such fees are not subject to a reduction under section 90-114 above; or (iii) where the governing body of the city does not approve a fee reduction with respect to a particular application, the property owner may apply to the city to pay such costs and fees in installments. The property owner's application to pay such costs and fees, or a portion thereof, in installments may be authorized if approved by the governing body of the city, subject to the following terms: (1)  The governing body of the city must determine, based upon the financial benefit determination, that the project would bring economic development to the city in the form of increased private sector employment, increased ad valorem tax revenue to the city, or increased net revenue to the city's utility system. (2)  The costs and fees may be amortized over such length of time as approved by the governing body of the city, but the repayment of such costs and fees may not be amortized over a period of more than seven years. (3)  The interest rate to be charged to a property owner in connection with the payment of such installment payments shall be as determined by the governing body of the city, taking into account the cost of funds to the city in connection with the project, current prevailing interest rates in the private sector, plus administrative costs and expenses incurred and to be incurred by the city in collecting and administering such installment payments. (4)  Such costs and fees to be paid in installments shall be repaid in equal monthly installments of principal and interest according to a written amortization schedule. At the time that the city and the property owner agree to the monthly repayment amounts, the property owner shall execute and deliver to the city the property owner's promissory note and such other documents as may be deemed necessary or appropriate to evidence such indebtedness and to secure the repayment thereof. In the event that the property owner is a utility customer of the city, the city shall be authorized to add the monthly installment payment to the monthly utility bill of the property owner or the property owner's tenant in the case of leased property. (5)  Prior to any installment payment being authorized under this section, the property owner must be determined by the governing body to be sufficiently creditworthy to insure to the governing body, to the extent reasonably possible, that the property owner will have the financial ability to pay such indebtedness within the term established by the city. (6)  The amount of the costs and fees to be paid in installments shall constitute a lien against the property of the property owner benefitted by such utility services until such time as all principal and interest are paid in full. Evidence of such lien shall be executed by the property owner and shall be recorded in the deed records in the Office the Clerk of the Superior Court of Sumter County, Georgia. The city clerk shall be authorized to cancel such lien upon the full payment thereof. Such liens shall be levied, enforced, and collected in the same manner as provided for the collection of city ad valorem taxes. (7)  Upon the sale, donation, gift, foreclosure, or the transfer of or operation of law of all or a portion of the real property subject to such lien, any remaining unpaid amounts of such costs and fees shall be due and payable in full at the time of such transfer unless the governing body of the city approves the assumption of such remaining obligations by the person or entity acquiring all or a portion of the subject property. (Ord. No. O-2013-24, 9-19-2013) 
Secs. 90-116—90-129. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - WATER SYSTEM 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
Sec. 90-130. - Access to private property; discovery of violations.     The public works employees, their agents and assistants may enter the premises of any water taker at any reasonable time to examine the pipes and fixtures, the quantity of water used; and the manner of its use and in case of fraudulent representation on the part of any water taker, or unnecessary waste of water, the payment will be forfeited and the supply of water stopped. (Code 1962, § 26-7; Code 1986, § 13-30) 
Secs. 90-131—90-158. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - RATES AND CHARGES; BILLING AND COLLECTION 
Sec. 90-159. - Meters—Required; installation and maintenance; cut off of service. (a)  All buildings, structures or premises supplied with water by the city waterworks shall be controlled by a meter. (b)  The meter shall be of the design and type to be approved by the utilities director or his designee, and shall be provided and installed by the city water department at a charge adequate to cover the purchase and installation costs of said meter. After installation, such meter shall be under the control of the water department of the city; and if such meter becomes damaged by the negligence of the property owner or tenant, the expense of any replacement or repair to such meter by the city water department shall be borne by the property owner; otherwise, the city water department shall replace any such meter at the city's expense when, in the judgment of the utilities director, or his designee, such meter is defective or in need of replacement. (c)  If any person shall refuse to comply with the provisions of this section, the supply of water to such service shall be cut off. (Code 1962, 26-11; Code 1986, § 13-20; Ord. No. O-92-08-24, 8-24-1992) 
Sec. 90-160. - Same—Separate connections; definitions; service charge formula for multiple use. (a)  Each house, store, building, place of business, or residential premises which desires to have water service shall have a separate meter and be separately connected to said meter, except as hereinafter provided. (b)  The term "residential premises" means: (1)  A single-family apartment unit; (2)  A single-family dwelling house; (3)  A single-family mobile home dwelling unit. (c)  Where a multiple residential premises is served through a master meter, the owner of the multiple residential premises shall be required to pay a base water charge for each single-family residential premises, and, in addition thereto, the owner shall also pay all charges for actual water used at the premises to be calculated based upon the current city water rate schedule as approved by the city council. (d)  Where a multiple residential premises is served through a master meter, the bill for such water charge, shall be to the owner of the property served by such master meter. (e)  The term "business premises" means a premises upon which a business is being conducted. (f)  The term "multiple-business premises" means a premises upon which two or more businesses are located. (g)  Where a multiple-business premises is served through a master meter, the owner of the multiple-business premises shall be required to pay a base water charge for each separate business location constituting said multiple business premises, whether occupied or not, located upon the multiple business premises, and, in addition thereto, said owner shall also pay all charges for actual water used at the premises to be calculated based upon the current city water rate schedule as approved by the city council. (h)  Where a multiple-business premises is served through a master meter, the bill for such water charge shall be to the owner of the property served by such master meter. (i)  A master meter will not be allowed to serve a multiple residential or business premises except in those instances where all of the premises of such multiple premises are under a single ownership. (j)  Notwithstanding the foregoing, where a newly constructed or renovated multiple residential premises is served through a master meter, for each unit actually rented during the first two months after completion of such construction or renovation, the owner shall only be required to pay a base water charge, plus payment for any water used. Such two-month period is to begin on the date the owner makes application for a sanitation receptacle for such premises. The electric utility providing service to the premises shall be contacted each month during such two-month period by the finance director's office to verify the actual number of units having electric power on the meter reading date. Such number of units having electric power on the meter reading date shall be deemed to be units actually rented for the purposes of this section. At the conclusion of said two-month period, the owner shall be required to pay a base water charge, plus any water used above or in excess of such base charge, for all units located at the premises, whether or not such units are rented. For purposes of this section, the term "renovated multiple residential premises" means a multiple residential premises renovated to such an extent that all tenants thereof were required to vacate the premises being renovated during the renovation process. (Code 1962, § 26-6; Code 1986, § 13-21; Ord. No. O-91-03-08, 3-25-1991; Ord. No. O-92-08-24, 8-24-1992) 
Sec. 90-161. - Same—Tampering with meter or lock. (a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to tamper with any water meter in the city so as to cause said meter to misregister or fail to register the volume of water furnished to the owner or user of water through said meter. (b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to tamper with any water meter or water meter lock in the city so as to cause the service to be cut back on when the city has terminated the service for a reason. (Code 1962, § 26-5; Code 1986, § 13-22; Ord. No. O-10-09-31, 9-20-2010) State Law reference— Theft of services, O.C.G.A. § 16-8-5. 
Sec. 90-162. - Tap charges and relocation of water meters. (a)  Water tap charges are as established by ordinance. The cost of installing a meter other than those listed by ordinance will be charged according to actual installation costs. (b)  There shall be a charge in the amount established by ordinance payable by the city's water customer any time that a water meter two inches or smaller in diameter is moved from one location to another location on such customer's property at the request of the customer. Such charge shall be paid by the customer at the time such service is provided, or shall be billed to the customer with the customer's regular monthly water bill, whichever is deemed appropriate by the city. (c)  In the event that a customer seeks to move a water meter from one location to another on such customer's water, and such water meter is two inches in diameter or greater, then such water meter must be moved, upon the approval of such a move by the city, by a private contractor licensed to undertake such activity. Such private contractor shall be either, hired by the customer or, if the customer so requests, the city will hire such private contractor. In the event that the city hires such private contractor, then the city will bill the customer on said customer's water bill for the contractor's charges for such work. In the event that the customer hires the contractor directly, then the customer shall pay the contractor's charges directly to the contractor. (Code 1962, § 26-1; Code 1986, § 13-23; Ord. No. O-89-03-06, 3-27-1989; Ord. No. O-90-12-31, 12-26-1990; Ord. No. O-00-07-32, 6-23-2000; Ord. No. O-03-08-19, 9-18-2003; Ord. No. O-04-11-29, 12-16-2004) 
Sec. 90-163. - Service deposit—Nonsingle-family, commercial and industrial customers; nonprofit organizations. (a)  All categories of consumers of water in the city other than single-family residences shall be required to pay a service deposit in the amount established by ordinance before water service is made available, and in the case of all existing commercial, industrial and other residential water customers an average will be taken of the previous customer's six months' water usage and the deposit required will be one month's bill to be computed and rounded off to the nearest dollar amount; and provided further, however, in the case of a previous consumption history not being available for a new commercial, industrial or nonsingle-family residential water customer, a monthly figure will be estimated, based on a similar type commercial, industrial or nonsingle-family water customer, and a followup computation will be done after six months' water usage to ascertain the accuracy of such estimated deposit amount charged, and an adjustment either up or down will be made at that time, based on the average six months' water usage. (b)  Nonprofit organizations shall be required to pay a service deposit calculated in the same manner as set out in subsection (a) of this section; provided, however, that the finance director shall be authorized to waive such service deposit for nonprofit organizations where the nonprofit organization has established its credit worthiness from such documentation or other information presented to the finance director. (c)  No facilities owned or operated by a government entity shall be required to pay any advance water service deposit. The term "facilities owned or operated by a government entity" shall include any such facilities owned or operated by a government and any boards, authorities, or divisions appointed or established by any governmental entity for the provision of public services as authorized by the constitution or laws of the state or federal government. (Code 1962, § 26-2; Code 1986, § 13-24; Ord. No. O-87-12-27, 12-21-1987; Ord. No. O-95-03-10, 3-23-1995; Ord. No. O-04-12-33, 12-16-2004; Ord. No. O-05-07-18, 7-21-2005) 
Sec. 90-164. - Same—Exceptions, refunds. (a)  An advance service deposit is required before water service is made available to consumers of water in the city. (b)  All residents except, those who have presented a letter from another utility company establishing their credit worthiness or has or have had a utility account in good standing with the city. For these customers, the advance service deposit may be waived by the finance director. (c)  The service deposit required of residential customers under subsection (a) of this section shall be refunded after the customer has maintained service at the same address for a minimum of 24 months with no delinquencies. The city utility billing department shall accomplish the refunding at least annually by applying the customer's deposit to his bill and notifying the customer when it has been done. (Code 1986, § 13-25; Ord. No. O-87-12-27, 12-21-1987; Ord. No. O-04-12-33, 12-16-2004) 
Sec. 90-165. - Water service rates—Inside city limits. (a)  Residential, small commercial, and large commercial users. Rates in the amount established by ordinance shall be charged for users inside the city limits for water service furnished to them by the city. (b)  Industrial users. Rates in the amount established by ordinance shall be charged for users inside the city limits for water service furnished to them by the city. (c)  Qualifying senior citizens. There shall be a ten percent discount applied to the rates referenced in subsection (a) of this section for qualifying senior citizens. A qualifying senior citizen is one who meets all of the following qualifications: (1)  They shall be 62 years of age or older. (2)  They shall have a total household income from all sources not exceeding $15,000.00. (3)  They shall complete and sign an application attesting certain required information. (4)  They shall have the utility account in the name of the qualifying senior citizen. (Code 1962, §§ 26-3, 26-22; Code 1986, § 13-26; Ord. of 12-22-1986, § (a); Ord. No. O-88-02-09, 2-22-1988; Ord. No. O-92-01-01, 1-28-1992; Ord. No. O-93-01-02, 1-26-1993; Ord. No. O-93-02-07, 2-22-1993; Ord. No. O-94-01-04, 1-25-1994; Ord. No. O-98-01-01, 1-22-1998; Ord. No. O-99-01-05, 12-17-1998; Ord. No. O-01-01-03, 1-18-2001; Ord. No. O-01-01-05, 1-18-2001; Ord. No. O-02-01-02, 1-24-2002; Ord. No. O-03-01-01, 1-23-2003; Ord. No. O-06-01-03, 1-19-2006) 
Sec. 90-166. - Same—Outside the city limits. (a)  In accord with the provisions of state law and the City's Charter, the city shall be authorized to provide water service to residential, small commercial, large commercial, and industrial users whose premises are located outside the corporate limits of the city. (b)  The water rates to be charged by the city for water service provided by the city to residential, small commercial, large commercial, and industrial users whose premises are located outside the corporate limits of the city shall be two times the rates charged for similar services to city water customers whose premises are located within the corporate limits of the city. (c)  The provision of such water services to premises located outside the corporate limits of the city shall only be authorized upon the occurrence of the following: (1)  The city shall have entered into an intergovernmental contract with the county authorizing the provision of water services in the unincorporated areas of the county as required pursuant to article IV, section II, paragraph III, subsection (b) of the Constitution of the State of Georgia of 1983, as such may be now or hereafter amended; and (2)  The owner of the premises to which such water services are proposed to be provided executes and delivers to the city a written contract between the city and such property owner, which contract shall provide, at a minimum, the method by which the property owner shall pay the city for base charges and water usage at the premises, the terms and conditions for the provision of such water services, and such other terms and conditions as the parties may deem appropriate in connection with such contract. In addition thereto, and as further consideration for the city's provision of water services to the property owner's premises outside the corporate limits of the city, said contract shall provide that in the event that the property owner's premises, or any portion thereof, becomes subject to annexation pursuant to the provisions of O.C.G.A. title 36, ch. 36, art. 2 (O.C.G.A. § 36-36-20 et seq.), annexation pursuant to application by 100 percent of landowners, then the property owner shall, within 90 calendar days after such premises become subject to such annexation, apply to the city for annexation of such premises into the city. Each party to the contract shall be responsible for undertaking all proceedings necessary in order to effect such annexation in accord with state law. Such contract shall also provide that upon the completion of such annexation, the water rates charged for the provision of water services to the premises shall be the same water rates as those rates charged to residential, small commercial, large commercial, or industrial users, as the case may be, which are located within the corporate limits of the city. (d)  Notwithstanding the foregoing, the rates for any water services provided by the city to facilities owned or operated by a government which are located outside the corporate limits shall be the same as such rates for water service customers located inside the corporate limits of the city. For such purposes, the term "facilities owned or operated by a government" shall include any such facilities owned or operated by a government or any boards, authorities, or divisions appointed or established by such government, for the provision of public services as authorized by the Constitution and the laws of the state or federal government. (e)  This section shall be applicable to any residential, small commercial, large commercial, or industrial users whose premises are located outside the corporate limits of the city that commence the use of city water services after August 1, 2005.
