All pollutant analyses, including sampling techniques, to be submitted as part of a wastewater discharge permit application or report shall be performed in accordance with the techniques prescribed in 40 CFR 136, unless otherwise specified in an applicable categorical pretreatment standard. If 40 CFR 136 does not contain sampling or analytical techniques for the pollutant in question, sampling and analysis must be performed in accordance with procedures approved by EPA. (11)  Sample collection. a.  Except as indicated in subsection (d)(11)b of this section, the user must collect wastewater samples using flow proportional composite collection techniques. In the event flow proportional sampling is infeasible, the city may authorize the use of time proportional sampling or a minimum of four grab samples where the user demonstrates that this will provide a representative sample of the effluent being discharged. In addition, grab samples may be required to show compliance with instantaneous discharge limits. b.  Samples for oil and grease, temperature, pH, cyanide, phenols, sulfide, and volatile organic compounds must be obtained using grab collection techniques. (12)  Timing. Written reports will be deemed, to have been submitted on the date postmarked. For reports, which are not mailed, postage prepaid, into a mail facility serviced by the United States Postal Service, the date of receipt of the report shall govern. (13)  Recordkeeping. Users subject to the reporting requirements of this division shall retain, and make available for inspection and copying, all records of information obtained pursuant to any monitoring activities required by this division and any additional records of information obtained pursuant to monitoring activities undertaken by the user independent of such requirements. Records shall include the date, exact place, method, and time of sampling, name of the person taking the samples; the dates analysis were performed; who performed the analysis; the analytical techniques or methods used; and the results of such analysis. These records shall remain available for a period of at least three years. This period shall be automatically extended for the duration of any litigation concerning the user or the city, or where the user has been specifically notified of a longer retention period by the city. (e)  Compliance monitoring. (1)  Right of entry; inspection and sampling. The city shall have the right to enter the premises of any user to determine whether the user is complying with all requirements of this division and any wastewater discharge permit or order issued hereunder. Users shall allow the city ready access to all parts of the premises for the purposes of inspection, sampling, records examination and copying, and the performance of any additional duties. a.  Where a user has security measures in force, which require proper identification and clearance before entry into its premises, the user shall make necessary arrangements with its security guards so that, upon presentation of suitable identification, the city personnel will be permitted to enter without delay for the purposes of performing specific responsibilities. b.  The city shall have the right to set up on the user's property, or require installation of, such devices as are necessary to conduct sampling and metering of the user's operations. c.  The city may require the user to install monitoring equipment as necessary. The facility's sampling and monitoring equipment shall be maintained at all times in a safe and proper operating condition by the user at its own expense. All devices used to measure wastewater flow and quality shall be calibrated on at least an annual basis to ensure their accuracy. d.  Any temporary or permanent obstruction to safe and easy access to the facility to be inspected and/or sampled shall be promptly removed by the user at the written or verbal request of the city and shall not be replaced. The costs of clearing such access shall be born by the user. e.  Unreasonable delays in allowing the city access to the user's premises shall be a violation of this division. (2)  Search warrants. If the city has been refused access to a building, structure, or property, or any part thereof, and is able to demonstrate probable cause to believe that there may be a violation of this division, or that there is need to inspect and sample as part of a routine inspection and sampling program of the city designed to verify compliance with this division or any permit or order issued hereunder, or to protect the overall public health, safety and welfare of the community, then the city may seek issuance of a search warrant from the municipal court of the city. (f)  Confidential information. Information and data on a user obtained from reports, questionnaires, permit applications, permits, monitoring programs, and from inspections shall be available to the public, EPD, EPA or other governmental agency without restriction unless the user specifically requests and is able to demonstrate to the satisfaction of the city, EPD, and EPA, that release of such information would divulge information, processes or methods of production entitled to protection as trade secrets of the user. Users wishing to keep such information confidential must assert a claim of confidentiality at the time the information is submitted to the city, such confidential information may be withheld from the public but it will always be made available to the EPD and EPA. Effluent data will be available to the public without restriction. (g)  Publication of significant noncompliance. The city shall publish annually, in the largest daily newspaper published in the city, a list of the users that, during the previous 12 months, were in significant noncompliance with applicable pretreatment standards and requirements. The term "significant noncompliance" means: (1)  Chronic violations of wastewater discharge limits, defined here as those in which 66 percent or more of wastewater measurements taken during a six-month period exceed the daily maximum limit or average limit for the same pollutant parameter by any amount; (2)  Technical review criteria (TRC) violations, defined here as those in which 33 percent or more of wastewater measurements taken for each pollutant parameter during a six-month period equals or exceeds the product of the daily maximum limit or the average limit multiplied by the applicable criteria; 1.4 for BOD, TSS, fats, oils and grease, and 1.2 for all other pollutants except pH; (3)  Any other discharge violation that the city believes has caused, alone or in combination with other discharges, interference or passthrough, including endangering the health of POTW personnel or the general public; (4)  Any discharge of pollutants that has caused imminent endangerment to the public or to the environment, or has resulted in the city's exercise of its emergency authority to halt or prevent such a discharge; (5)  Failure to meet, within 90 days of the scheduled date, a compliance schedule milestone contained in a wastewater discharge permit or enforcement order for starting construction, completing construction, or attaining final compliance; (6)  Failure to provide within 30 days after the due date, any required reports, including baseline monitoring reports, reports on compliance with categorical pretreatment standard deadlines, periodic self-monitoring reports, and reports on compliance with compliance schedules; (7)  Failure to accurately report noncompliance; or (8)  Any other violation, which the city determines, will adversely affect the operation or implementation of the local pretreatment program. (h)  Service charges. The city may adopt charges and fees, which may include: (1)  Fees for reimbursement of costs of setting up and operating the city's pretreatment program; (2)  Fees for monitoring, inspections and surveillance procedures; (3)  Fees for reviewing accidental discharge procedures and construction; (4)  Fees for permit applications; (5)  Fees for filing appeals; (6)  Fees for consistent removal, by the city, of pollutants otherwise subject to federal pretreatment standards; (7)  Other fees as the city may deem necessary to carry out the requirements contained herein. These fees relate solely to the matters covered by this division and are separate from all other fees chargeable by the city. The applicable charges shall be set forth in the city's schedule of charges and fees. (Code 1986, § 13-87; Ord. No. O-98-05-19, 5-21-1998) 
Sec. 90-259. - Administrative enforcement remedies. (a)  Notification of violation. Whenever the city finds that any user has violated or is violating this division, or a wastewater permit or order issued hereunder, the utilities director or his agent may serve upon said user written notice of violation. Within ten days of the receipt date of this notice, an explanation of the violation and a plan for the satisfactory correction and prevention thereof, to include specific required actions, shall be submitted to the utilities director or his agent. Submission of this plan in no way relieves the user of liability for any violations occurring before or after receipt of the notice of violation. (b)  Consent orders. The utilities director is hereby empowered to enter into consent orders, assurances of voluntary compliance, or other similar documents establishing an agreement with the user to correct the noncompliance within a time period also specified by the order. Consent orders shall have the same force and effect as compliance orders issued pursuant to subsection (d) of this section. (c)  Show cause hearing. The utilities director may order any user which causes or contributes to a violation of this division or wastewater permit or order issued hereunder, to show cause why a proposed enforcement action should not be taken. The notice of the hearing shall be served personally or by registered or certified mail, return receipt requested, at least ten days prior to the hearing. Such notice may be served on any user. Whether or not a duly notified user appears as noticed, immediate enforcement action may be pursued. (d)  Compliance order. When the utilities director finds that a user has violated or continues to violate this division or a permit or order issued thereunder, he may issue an order to the user responsible for the discharge directing that, following a specified time period, sewer service shall be discontinued unless adequate treatment facilities, devices, or other related appurtenances have been installed and are properly operated. Orders may also contain such other requirements as might be reasonably necessary and appropriate to address the noncompliance, including the installation of pretreatment technology, additional self-monitoring, and management practices. (e)  Cease and desist orders. When the utilities director finds that a user has violated or continues to violate this division or any permit or order issued hereunder, the utilities director may issue an order to cease and desist all such violations and direct those persons in noncompliance to: (1)  Comply forthwith; (2)  Take such appropriate remedial or preventive action as may be needed to properly address a continuing or threatened violation, including halting operations and terminating the discharge. (f)  Administrative fines. Notwithstanding any other section of this division, any user who is found to have violated any provision of this division, or permits or orders issued hereunder, shall be fined in an amount not to exceed $1,000.00 per violation. Each day on which noncompliance shall occur or continue shall be deemed a separate and distinct violation. Such assessments may be added to the user's next scheduled sewer service charge and the city shall have such other collection remedies as it needs to collect other individual user's property. Users desiring to dispute such fines must file a request for the city to reconsider the fine within ten days of being notified of the fine. Where the utilities director believes a request has merit, he shall convene a hearing on the matter within 15 days of receiving the request from the industrial user. (g)  Emergency suspensions. (1)  The utilities director may suspend the wastewater treatment service and wastewater permit of a user whenever such suspension is necessary in order to stop an actual or threatened discharge presenting or causing imminent or substantial endangerment to the health or welfare of persons, the POTW, or the environment. (2)  Any user notified of a suspension of the wastewater treatment service and/or the wastewater permit shall immediately stop or eliminate its contribution. In the event of a user's failure to immediately comply voluntarily with the suspension order, the utilities director shall take such steps as deemed necessary, including immediate severance of the sewer connection, to prevent or minimize damage to the POTW, its receiving stream, or endangerment to any individuals. The utilities director shall allow the user to recommence its discharge when the endangerment has passed, unless termination proceedings set forth in subsection (h) of this section are initiated against the user. A user who is the subject of a suspension order under this subsection shall have the right to appeal to the utilities director from such suspension, but such suspension shall remain in full force and effect pending such hearing and the decision of the director thereto. (3)  A user which is responsible, in whole or in part, for imminent endangerment shall submit a detailed written statement describing the causes of the harmful contribution and the measures taken to prevent any future occurrence to the utilities director prior to the date of the hearing described in subsection (g)(2) of this section. (h)  Termination of permit. Significant industrial users proposing to discharge into the POTW, must first obtain a wastewater discharge permit from the public works department. Any user who violates the following conditions of this division or a wastewater discharge permit or order, or any applicable state and federal law, is subject to permit termination: (1)  Violation of permit conditions; (2)  Failure to accurately report the wastewater constituents and characteristics of its discharge; (3)  Failure to report significant changes in operations or wastewater constituents and characteristics; or (4)  Refusal of reasonable access to the user's premises for the purpose of inspection, monitoring, or sampling. Any noncompliant industrial users will be notified of the proposed termination of their wastewater permit and will be offered an opportunity to show cause under subsection (c) of this section, why the proposed action should not be taken. (i)  Termination of services. The city may order any user who causes or continues to allow an unauthorized discharge to enter the POTW to show cause before the city council as to why termination of services should not happen. A notice shall be served on the user specifying the time and place of a hearing to be held by the city council regarding the termination of services, the reasons why the action is to be taken, and directing the user to show cause before the city council why the proposed enforcement action should not be taken. The notice of the hearing shall be served by registered or certified mail, return receipt requested, at least ten days before the hearing. Service may be made on any agent or officer of a corporation. The city council may itself conduct the hearing and take the evidence, or may designate any of its members or any officer or employee of the public works to: (1)  Issue in the name of the city council notices of the hearing requesting the attendance and testimony of witnesses and the production of evidence relevant to any matter involved in such hearings; (2)  Take the evidence; (3)  Transmit a report of the evidence and hearing, including transcripts and other evidence, together with recommendations to the city council for action thereon. At any hearing held pursuant to this division, testimony must be taken under oath and recorded stenographically. The transcript, so recorded, will be made available to any member of the public or any party to the hearing upon payment of the usual charges thereof. (j)  Order from city council to discontinue service. After the city council has reviewed the evidence, it may issue an order to the user responsible for the discharge directing that, following a specified time period, the sewer service is to be discontinued unless adequate treatment facilities, devices, or other related appurtenances are properly operated. Further orders and directives as are necessary and appropriate may be issued. (Code 1986, § 13-88; Ord. No. O-98-05-19, 5-21-1998) 
Sec. 90-260. - Judicial remedies.     If any person discharges sewage, industrial wastes, or other wastes into the wastewater disposal system contrary to the provisions of this division or any order or permit issued hereunder, the utilities director, through the city attorney, may commence an action for appropriate legal and/or equitable relief in a court of competent jurisdiction. (1)  Injunctive relief. Whenever a user has violated or continues to violate this division or any order or permit issued hereunder, the city, through counsel may petition the court for its issuance of a preliminary or permanent injunction or both, as may be appropriate, which restrains or compels the activities on the part of the user. The city may also initiate nuisance abatement proceedings in the municipal court of the city, as an alternate remedy. (2)  Civil penalties. a.  Any user who has violated or continues to violate this division or any order or permit issued hereunder, shall be liable to the city for a civil penalty of up to at least $1,000.00 plus actual damages incurred by the POTW per violation per day for as long as the violation continues. In addition to the above described penalty and damages, the city may recover reasonable attorneys' fees, court costs, and other expenses associated with the enforcement activities, including sampling and monitoring expenses. b.  The city shall petition the municipal court of the city or any state court having jurisdiction to impose, assess, and recover such sums. In determining the amount of liability, the municipal court of the city or any state court having jurisdiction shall take into account all relevant circumstances, including, but not limited to, the extent of harm caused by the violation, the magnitude and duration, any economic benefit gained through the user's violation, corrective actions by the user, the compliance history of the user, and any other factors as justice requires. (3)  Criminal prosecution. a.  Any user who willfully or negligently violates any provision of this division or any orders or permits issued hereunder shall, upon conviction in the municipal court of the city, be guilty of a misdemeanor. b.  Any user who knowingly makes any false statements, representations, or certifications in any application, record, report, plan or other document filed or required to be maintained pursuant to this division, or wastewater permit, or who falsifies, tampers with, or knowingly renders inaccurate any monitoring device or method required under this division shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. (Code 1986, § 13-89; Ord. No. O-98-05-19, 5-21-1998) 
Sec. 90-261. - Supplemental enforcement remedies. (a)  Performance bonds. The utilities director may decline to reissue a permit to any industrial user which has failed to comply with the provisions of this division or any order or previous permit issued hereunder unless such user files with it a satisfactory bond, payable to the city, in a sum not to exceed a value determined by the utilities director to be necessary to achieve consistent compliance. (b)  Liability insurance. The utilities director may decline to reissue a permit to any industrial user which has failed to comply with the provisions of this division or any order or previous permit issued hereunder, unless the industrial user first submits proof that it has obtained financial assurances sufficient to restore or repair POTW damage caused by its discharge. (c)  Water supply severance. Whenever an industrial user has been found after a hearing, to be in violation of the provisions of this division or an order issued hereunder, water service to the industrial user may be severed and service will only recommence, at the user's expense, after it has satisfactorily demonstrated its ability to comply. (Code 1986, § 13-90; Ord. No. O-98-05-19, 5-21-1998) 
Sec. 90-262. - Affirmative defenses. (a)  Treatment upsets. (1)  For the purposes of this division, the term "upset" means an exceptional incident in which there is unintentional and temporary noncompliance with categorical pretreatment standards because of factors beyond the reasonable control of the user. An upset does not include noncompliance to the extent caused by operational error, improperly designed treatment facilities, inadequate treatment facilities, lack of preventative maintenance, or careless or improper operation. (2)  An upset shall constitute an affirmative defense to an action brought for noncompliance with categorical pretreatment standards if the requirements of subsection (a)(3) of this section are met. (3)  A user who wishes to establish the affirmative defense of upset shall demonstrate, through properly signed, contemporaneous operating logs, or other relevant evidence that: a.  An upset occurred and the user can identify the cause of the upset; b.  The facility was at the time being operated in a prudent and workmanlike manner and in compliance with applicable operation and maintenance procedures; and c.  The user has submitted the following information to the utilities director within 24 hours of becoming aware of the upset, if this information is provided orally, a written submission must be provided within five days: 1.  A description of the indirect discharge and cause of noncompliance; 2.  The period of noncompliance, including exact dates and times or, if not corrected, the anticipated time the noncompliance is expected to continue; and 3.  Steps being taken and the plan to reduce, eliminate, and prevent recurrence of the noncompliance. (4)  In any enforcement proceeding, the user seeking to establish the occurrence of an upset shall have the burden of proof. (5)  Users will have the opportunity for a judicial determination on any claim of upset only in an enforcement action brought for noncompliance with categorical pretreatment standards. (6)  Users shall control production of all discharges, to the extent necessary to maintain compliance with categorical pretreatment standards upon reduction, loss, or failure of its treatment facility until the facility is restored or an alternative method of treatment is provided. This requirement applies in the situation where, among other things, the primary source of power of the treatment facility is reduced, lost, or fails. (b)  Treatment bypasses. (1)  For the purposes of this division: a.  The term "bypass" means the intentional diversion of wastestreams from any portion of a user's treatment facility. b.  The term "severe property damage" means substantial physical damage to property, damage to the treatment facilities which causes them to become inoperable, or substantial and permanent loss of natural resources which can reasonably be expected to occur in the absence of a bypass. Severe property damage does not mean economic loss caused by delays in production. (2)  A user may allow any bypass to occur which does not cause pretreatment standards or requirements to be violated, but only if it also is for essential maintenance to ensure efficient operation. These bypasses are not subject to the provision of subsection (b)(3) and (4) of this section. (3)  Need for bypass known in advance. a.  If a user knows in advance of the need for a bypass, it shall submit prior notice to the utilities director, at least ten days before the date of the bypass, if possible. b.  A user shall submit oral notice to the utilities director of an anticipated bypass that exceeds applicable pretreatment standards within 24 hours from the time it becomes aware of the bypass. A written submission shall also be provided within five days of the time the user becomes aware of the bypass. The written submission shall contain a description of the bypass and its cause; the duration of the bypass, including exact dates and times, and, if the bypass has not been corrected, the anticipated time it is expected to continue; and steps taken or planned to reduce, eliminate, and prevent reoccurrence of the bypass. The utilities director may waive the written report on a case-by-case basis if the oral report has been received within 24 hours. (4)  A bypass is prohibited, and the utilities director may take an enforcement action against a user for a bypass, unless: a.  The bypass was unavoidable to prevent loss of life, personal injury, or severe property damage; b.  There were no feasible alternatives to the bypass, such as the use of auxiliary treatment facilities, retention of untreated wastes, or maintenance during normal periods of equipment downtime. This condition is not satisfied if adequate backup equipment should have been installed in the exercise of reasonable engineering judgment to prevent a bypass which occurred during normal periods of equipment downtime or preventative maintenance; c.  The user submitted notices as required under subsection (b)(3) of this section; and d.  The utilities director may approve an anticipated bypass, after considering its adverse effects, if the utilities director determines that it will meet the three conditions listed in this subsection (b)(4). (c)  Prohibited discharge standards. A user shall have an affirmative defense to an enforcement action brought against it for noncompliance with the general prohibitions in section 90-256 or the specific prohibitions in subsections 90-256(d)(1)—(13), if it can prove that it did not know, or have reason to know, that its discharge, alone or in conjunction with discharges from other sources, would cause passthrough or interference and that either: (1)  A local limit exists for each pollutant discharged and the user was in compliance with each limit directly prior to, and during, the passthrough or interference; or (2)  No local limit exists, but the discharge did not change substantially in nature or constituents from the user's prior discharge when the city was regularly in compliance with its NPDES permit, and in the case of interference, was in compliance with applicable sludge use or disposal requirements. (Code 1986, § 13-91; Ord. No. O-98-05-19, 5-21-1998) 
Secs. 90-263—90-287. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - RATES AND CHARGES; BILLING AND COLLECTIONS 
Sec. 90-288. - No free service; connections to be effectuated; meters required. (a)  No free service shall at any time be furnished from the system and the city shall undertake within its health powers, or such applicable powers now or hereafter provided by law, to have each separate improved real property within the corporate limits of the city, as now existent and as the same may hereafter be extended, connected to the sewerage facilities. (b)  The city shall endeavor to prohibit the disposal of sewage by any other means. (c)  No customer shall be connected to the system or served by the city without a proper meter having been first installed. (d)  All services shall be furnished in accordance with rates now or hereafter established, including services furnished to any county, municipal corporation or any other public board or body. (Code 1962, § 26-23; Code 1986, § 13-60) 
Sec. 90-289. - Sewer tap and connection charges established. (a)  Sewer tap charges are as established by ordinance. The cost of installing a meter other than those listed by ordinance will be charged according to actual installation costs. (b)  The cost of connection to sewer shall be as established by ordinance. (Code 1962, § 26-21; Code 1986, § 13-61; Ord. No. O-99-12-46, 12-16-1999; Ord. No. O-04-11-29, 12-16-2004) 
Sec. 90-290. - Service charge rates; inside city limits. (a)  Residential, small commercial, and large commercial users. Rates in the amount established by ordinance shall be charged for users inside the city limits for sewer service furnished to them by the city. (b)  Residential sewer rate computation. Residential sewer rates shall be based upon the actual water usage each monthly billing cycle and shall be computed at the current rates for the applicable monthly sewer billing cycle. (c)  Industrial users. Rates in the amount established by ordinance shall be charged for users inside the city limits for sewer service furnished to them by the city. (d)  Industrial sewer rate computation . Any industry that has received approval from the utilities director and has installed a flow meter for the purposes of metering wastewater shall be billed in the amount established by ordinance. (Code 1962, § 26-22; Code 1986, § 13-62; Ord. of 12-22-1986, § (b); Ord. No. O-88-04-16, 4-25-1988; Ord. No. O-89-01-01, 1-23-1989; Ord. No. O-89-12-41, 12-18-1989; Ord. No. O-90-12-35, 12-26-1990; Ord. No. O-92-01-02, 1-28-1992; Ord. No. O-93-01-03, 1-28-1993; Ord. No. O-94-01-05, 1-25-1994; Ord. No. O-96-01-04, 1-25-1996; Ord. No. O-98-01-02, 1-22-1998; Ord. No. O-99-01-06, 12-17-1998; Ord. No. O-01-01-04, 1-18-2001; Ord. No. O-02-01-03, 1-24-2002; Ord. No. O-03-01-02, 1-23-2003; Ord. No. O-06-01-04, 1-19-2006; Ord. No. O-2015-18, 11-19-2015) 
Sec. 90-291. - Sewer rates and contract for sewer usage; outside the city limits. (a)  In accord with the provisions of state law and the city's Charter, the city shall be authorized to provide sewer service to residential, small commercial, large commercial, and industrial users whose premises are located outside the corporate limits of the city. (b)  The sewer rates to be charged by the city for sewer service provided by the city to residential, small commercial, large commercial, and industrial users located outside the corporate limits of the city shall be two times the rates charged for similar services to city sewer customers whose premises are located within the corporate limits of the city. (c)  The provision of such sewer services outside the corporate limits of the city shall only be authorized upon the occurrence of the following: (1)  The city shall have entered into an intergovernmental contract with the county authorizing the provision of sewer services in the unincorporated areas of the county as required pursuant to article IX, section II, paragraph III, subsection (b) of the Constitution of the State of Georgia of 1983, as such may be now or hereafter amended; and (2)  The owner of the premises, to which such sewer services are proposed to be provided, executes and delivers to the city a written contract between the city and such property owner, which contract shall provide, at a minimum, the method by which the property owner shall pay the city for base charges and sewer usage at the premises, the terms and conditions for the provision of such sewer services, and such other terms and conditions as the parties may deem appropriate with such contract. In addition thereto, and as further consideration for the city's provision of sewer services to the property owner's premises, said contract shall provide that in the event that the property owner's premises, or any portion thereof, becomes subject to annexation pursuant to the provisions of O.C.G.A. title 36, ch. 36, art. 2 (O.C.G.A. § 36-36-20 et seq.), annexation pursuant to application by 100 percent of landowners, then the property owner shall, within 90 calendar days after such premises become subject to such annexation, apply to the city for annexation of such premises into the city. Each party shall be responsible to undertake all proceedings necessary in order to effect such annexation in accord with state law. Such contract shall also provide that upon the completion of such annexation, the sewer rates charged for the provision of sewer services to the premises shall be the same sewer rates as those rates charged to residential, small commercial, large commercial, or industrial users, as the case may be, which are located within the corporate limits of the city. (d)  Notwithstanding the foregoing, the rates for any sewer services provided by the city to facilities owned or operated by a government which are located outside the corporate limits shall be the same as such rates for sewer service customers located inside the corporate limits of the city. For such purposes, the term "facilities owned or operated by a government" shall include any such facilities owned or operated by a government or any boards, authorities, or divisions appointed or established by such government, for the provision of public services as authorized by the Constitution and the laws of the state or federal government. (e)  This section shall be applicable to any residential, small commercial, large commercial, or industrial users whose premises are located outside the corporate limits of the city who commence the use of city sewer services after August 1, 2005. For residential customers whose premises are located outside the corporate limits of the city who are already city sewer customers prior to August 1, 2005, the rates for such sewer service provided by the city to such residential customers shall continue to be two times the rate charged for similar services for customers residing within the corporate limits of the city, but no contract or other agreement with respect to such residence shall be required. (Code 1962, § 26-4; Code 1986, § 13-63; Ord. No. O-85-05-12, 5-27-1985; Ord. No. O-84-03-05b, 3-27-1989; Ord. No. O-92-01-04, 1-28-1992; Ord. No. O-05-08-21, 8-18-2005) 
Sec. 90-292. - Nonusers of public water supply—Advance payment of service charges.     An advance sewer service payment in the amount established by ordinance is required before sanitary sewer service is furnished to any user of the city's sanitary sewer system whose premises is in the city and whose premises is not served by the public water supply system of the city. The deposit for users outside the city shall be as established by ordinance. (Code 1962, § 26-18.1; Code 1986, § 13-64; Ord. No. O-85-05-12, 5-27-1985) 
Sec. 90-293. - Same—Monthly charges. (a)  All occupants of premises located in the city served by the sanitary sewer system of the city, where such premises are not served by the public water system of the city, shall pay a monthly sanitary service charge. Such charge shall be determined with reference to a water meter installed at the expense of the owner at such location, which water meter shall be read at least monthly by the city. The charges shall include the base customer fee plus the operating fee specified in section 90-290, based upon water usage per month. In the event that said premises are located outside the city, the rates shall be specified in section 90-291. (b)  The owner of such premises shall be required to install a water meter at such location and in such proximity to the premises' water well as may be determined proper by the city. The water meter shall be installed in such a manner and in such location so as to require that all water usage at said premises is recorded by said meter. (Code 1962, § 26-16; Code 1986, § 13-65; Ord. No. O-90-04-10, 4-24-1990) 
Sec. 90-294. - Same—Charge imposed upon each family unit.     For the purpose of sections 90-292 and 90-293, the term "premises" is defined to be a single-family unit. Each additional family unit shall be charged a monthly service charge in the same amount. (Code 1962, § 26-17; Code 1986, § 13-66) 
Sec. 90-295. - Same—Charge imposed upon commercial unit.     A commercial unit which is now tied to the sanitary sewer system and which is not receiving water from the municipal system shall be charged a monthly sanitary sewer service charge in the amount as set out in section 90-293 and any industrial waste charges imposed. (Code 1962, § 26-18; Code 1986, § 13-67) 
Sec. 90-296. - Effect of nonpayment; disconnection of service.     Upon any occupant failing or refusing to pay the monthly sanitary sewer service charge after having been duly billed for same by the city, and following the lapse of 30 days after such billing, shall be deemed guilty of a violation of this division and the sanitary sewer service to such premises shall be terminated by the city severing the sanitary sewer connection at the property line. (Code 1962, § 26-19; Code 1986, § 13-68) 
Sec. 90-297. - Reinstatement of service; reconnection fee.     The sanitary sewer service will be reinstated by the city at such premises upon the occupant of the premises paying all past due sanitary sewer service charges billed to the occupant of said premises, together with a reconnection fee in the amount established by ordinance. (Code 1962, § 26-20; Code 1986, § 13-69) 
Sec. 90-298. - Billing.     The charges for such sewer services as aforesaid shall be included in the bill for charges for water services and facilities and shall be billed to the customers at the same time and in the same manner as now provided for the payment of water bills and same shall be collected in the manner and subject to the provisions applicable to the water bills. (Code 1962, § 26-24; Code 1986, § 13-70) 
Sec. 90-299. - Amending rates.     Nothing herein contained shall be construed as relieving the city of the requirement, as often as it may be necessary, to revise and adjust its schedule of rates, fees and charges for either water or sewer services and facilities, or both, as provided and covenanted in the ordinances of its city council heretofore or hereafter adopted authorizing the issuance of the city's water and sewerage revenue obligations. (Code 1962, § 26-25; Code 1986, § 13-71) 
Sec. 90-300. - Disposing of sewage by delivery to city facility.     All persons disposing of sewage by delivering same to the city sewage treatment facility shall be charged an amount established by ordinance. Said persons shall be billed on a monthly basis. (Code 1962, § 26-26; Code 1986, § 13-72) 
Secs. 90-301—90-318. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - NATURAL GAS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
Secs. 90-319—90-339. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - RATES AND CHARGES; BILLING AND COLLECTION 
Sec. 90-340. - Meters—Required; installation and maintenance; cut off of service. (a)  All buildings, structures or premises supplied with gas by the city gas system shall be controlled by a meter. (b)  The meter shall be of the design, type and size to be approved by the natural gas services director of the city and shall be provided and installed by the city gas department at a charge adequate to cover the purchase and installation costs of said meter. After installation, such meter shall be under the control of the gas department of the city; and if such meter becomes damaged by negligence of the property owner or tenant, the expense of any replacement or repair to such meter by the city gas department shall be borne by the property owner; otherwise, the city gas department will replace any such meter at the city's expense when, in the judgment of the city gas department, such meter is defective or in need of replacement. (c)  If any person shall refuse to comply with the provisions of this section, the supply of gas to such service shall be cut off. (Code 1986, § 13-100) 
Sec. 90-341. - Same—Separate connections.     Each house, store, building, place of business, or residential premises which desires to have gas service shall have a separate meter and be separately connected to said meter, except as hereinafter provided. (Code 1986, § 13-101) 
Sec. 90-342. - Same—Tampering with meter or lock. (a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to tamper with any gas meter in the city so as to cause said meter to misregister or fail to register the volume of gas furnished to the owner or user of gas through said meter. (b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to tamper with any gas meter lock in the city so as to cause the service to be cut back on when the city has terminated the service for a reason. (Code 1986, § 13-102) State Law reference— Theft of service, O.C.G.A. § 16-8-5. 
Sec. 90-343. - Service deposit—Nonsingle-family, commercial and industrial customers; nonprofit organizations. (a)  All categories of consumers of gas in the city other than single-family residences shall be required to pay a minimum amount established by ordinance as a service deposit before gas service is made available, and in the case of all existing commercial, industrial and other residential gas customers an average will be taken of the previous customer's six months of gas usage and the deposit required will be one month's bill to be computed and rounded off to the nearest dollar amount; and provided further, however, in the case of a previous consumption history not being available for a new commercial, industrial or nonsingle-family residential gas customer, a monthly figure will be estimated, based on a similar type commercial, industrial or nonsingle-family gas customer, and a followup computation will be calculated after six months of gas usage to ascertain the accuracy of such estimated deposit amount charged, and an adjustment either up or down will be made at that time, based on the average six months of gas usage. (b)  Nonprofit organizations shall be required to pay a service deposit calculated in the same manner as set out in subsection (a) of this section; provided, however, that the finance director shall be authorized to waive such service deposit for nonprofit organizations where the nonprofit organization has established its credit worthiness from such documentation or other information presented to the finance director. (Code 1986, § 13-103; Ord. No. O-87-12-27, 12-21-1987; Ord. No. O-95-03-10, 3-23-1995; Ord. No. O-04-12-33, 12-16-2004) 
Sec. 90-344. - Same—Exceptions, refunds. (a)  An advance service deposit in the amount established by ordinance is required before gas service is made available to the consumers of gas in the city, except those who have presented a letter from another utility company establishing their credit worthiness or have had a utility account in good standing with the city. For these customers, the advance service deposit may be waived by the finance director. (b)  The service deposit required of residential customers under subsection (a) of this section shall be refunded after the customer has maintained service at the same address for a minimum of 24 months with no delinquencies. The city utility billing department shall accomplish the refunding at least annually by applying the customer's deposit to his bill and notifying the customer when it has been done. (Code 1986, § 13-104; Ord. No. O-87-12-27, 12-21-1987; Ord. No. O-04-12-33, 12-16-2004) 
Sec. 90-345. - Senior citizens' discount on residential gas bill. (a)  A qualifying senior citizen is one who meets the following criteria: (1)  Shall be 62 years of age or older. (2)  Total household income from all sources shall not exceed $15,000.00. (3)  Shall complete and sign an application attesting certain required information. (4)  Shall have the residential utility account in the name of the qualifying senior citizen. (b)  The qualifying senior citizen shall be billed gas rates which are ten percent less than the current residential gas rates in effect. (Code 1986, § 13-105; Ord. No. O-93-02-08, 3-26-1993; Ord. No. O-01-01-05, 1-18-2001) 
Sec. 90-346. - Purchase gas adjustment. (a)  The customer rates for all classifications of firm natural gas customers are based upon the city's paying a commodity charge to the natural gas supplier. Under applicable federal statutes and regulations; namely the Federal Energy Regulatory Commission's Regulation section 154.38(d)(4), regulations under the Natural Gas Act and section 282.601 of the regulations under the Natural Gas Policy Act of 1978, the commodity charges imposed upon the city by the supplier have been rapidly increasing and otherwise fluctuating. Such rapid product cost fluctuations make it practically impossible for the city to establish firm natural gas customer rates at realistic levels to ensure normal revenues that will cover the purchase cost of gas, distribution and transportation costs, natural gas department operating expenses, and an established margin. (b)  To provide for fluctuations in the city's cost of natural gas purchased and other costs to the city that may be incurred in the delivery of natural gas to the city gate, the rates for firm natural gas imposed upon the various classifications of natural gas customers shall be subject to a purchase gas adjustment (hereinafter called "PGA") that will be calculated in accordance with subsection (d) of this section. (c)  The PGA shall not be reflected separately on the utility customer's monthly billing. (d)  The PGA shall be supplied on a monthly basis by the Municipal Gas Authority of Georgia (MGAG) to the city. The natural gas variable rates for all classifications of firm delivery customers shall be calculated monthly and shall be equal to the cost of gas plus the PGA plus the operating expenses and the appropriate rate of return on the city's investments in the natural gas system as determined by the city council from time to time. The Municipal Gas Authority of Georgia will provide the cost of natural gas each month prior to the city's billing cycle. In establishing the PGA, all fractions of cents shall be rounded up to the nearest whole cent. (e)  The city shall have available in the office of the finance director the applicable PGA and corresponding rates for the current calendar month and for the previous 24 calendar months so that interested parties may determine fluctuations in the city's natural gas rates to all classifications of firm load customers. (f)  Anything contained herein to the contrary notwithstanding, the city shall not consider any price fluctuations in its cost for propane in determining the purchase gas adjustment under this section unless the price fluctuations negatively impact the city's overall gross margin. (Code 1986, § 13-106; Ord. No. O-97-01-01, 1-23-1997; Ord. No. O-04-12-33, 12-16-2004) 
Sec. 90-347. - Discontinuance of service for failure to pay natural gas bill; reconnection charges.     All natural gas charges must be promptly paid or natural gas service will be discontinued and a reconnection fee in an amount established by ordinance shall be charged for turning the natural gas service on again. In addition, the current advance natural gas service payment required shall be paid in full to the city before the city shall turn the natural gas service on again in the event of a disconnection. (Ord. No. O-09-03-07, 3-19-2009) 
Sec. 90-348. - Reconnection of natural gas services after business hours.     In addition to the provisions of section 90-170 of this article, any person whose natural gas service has been turned off for nonpayment, or for other violation or violations of the City Code, and who requests reconnection services which must be performed after normal business hours, which are Monday—Friday 8:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m., shall be required to sign an "after hours service agreement" with the city before the reconnection services will be performed by the city. Such agreement shall provide that the customer requesting reconnection services must pay the service agreement fee, reconnection fees, and any past due amounts by 10:00 a.m., on the next business day. In the event that the customer does not pay such amounts within such time frame in violation of the agreement, the city shall be authorized to disconnect the natural gas for such customer again, and the charges incurred for the reconnection shall be added to the customer's natural gas service account. In the event that the customer fails to pay the amounts due under the after hours service agreement prior to the deadline for payment thereof, service shall not be reinstated for the customer all amounts owed by the customer to the city in connection with the customer's natural gas service are paid in full. In the event that the original disconnection is deemed to be an error on the part of the city, the service agreement fee and the reconnection fees will be waived. The amount of the service agreement fee and reconnection fees shall be established by ordinance. (Ord. No. O-09-03-07, 3-19-2009) 
Secs. 90-349—90-364. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - SOLID WASTE[3] Footnotes: --- (3) --- State Law reference— Solid Waste Management Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-20 et seq.; hazardous waste disposal, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-61 et seq.; Litter Control Law, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-4. 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
Sec. 90-365. - Definitions.     The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:     Ashes means and includes the waste product from coal, wood or other fuels used for cooking and heating.     Brown goods includes such items as chairs, mattresses, sofas, tables and other furniture items.     Building refuse means solid waste generated from construction or demolition activities undertaken on property located within the corporate limits of the city. The term "building refuse" includes, but is not limited to, lumber, brick, block, stone, carpet, plumbing materials, plaster, concrete, roofing, floor tile, gutters, and other substances accumulated as a result of construction of or repairs or additions to structures or accessory structures or the demolition thereof.     Bulk waste means appliances, furniture, bedding material, automobile parts, mechanical equipment, mechanical parts and carpet.     Commercial solid waste means all types of solid waste generated by stores, offices, restaurants, warehouses, and other nonmanufacturing activities, excluding residential and industrial wastes.     Composting means the controlled biological decomposition of organic matter into a stable, odor-free humus.     Disposable trash containers means plastic bags and cardboard, wooden and corrugated boxes which shall be nonreturnable and shall be collected and packed into the garbage truck collecting such items.     Disposal facility means any facility or location where the final deposition of solid waste occurs and includes, but is not limited to, landfilling and solid waste thermal treatment technology facilities.     Dump means to throw, discard, place, deposit, discharge, bury, burn or dispose of a substance.     Front-loading container means a heavy-duty steel container designed for use in commercial, industrial, and apartment units for storage of garbage, miscellaneous rubbish, trash and other waste.     Garbage means all vegetable and animal matter, food and other refuse from a kitchen, market, store, or elsewhere, including all matter that decays, attracts flies, and creates disagreeable odors.     Hazardous waste means solid or liquid waste material resulting from the manufacture or use of chemicals, pesticides and drugs, other than normal household use, pathological waste, highly flammable, explosive waste, toxic waste, sewer sludge, insecticides, poisons, corrosives, caustics, acids, infectious materials, compressed gases, biological materials, radioactive materials, petroleum products and other waste material that is determined to be a hazard to public health, safety or environment.     Industrial waste means solid waste from generated by factories, processing plants, wholesale establishments, assembling plants, food processing wastes, cinders and ashes, lumber scraps, sawdust, shavings, including solids, semisolids, sludges, and liquids floor sweepings, metal scrap and shavings, and any other waste products from industrial and manufacturing processes.     Leachate collection system means a system at a landfill for collection of the leachate, which may percolate through the waste and into the soils surrounding the landfill.     Litter means all discarded manmade materials, including, but not limited to, garbage, lottery tickets, household trash, industrial waste, building materials, appliances, or portions thereof, refuse, waste materials, sand, gravel, slag, brick bats, rubbish, tin cans, cigarette and cigar butts, other tobacco products, rags, cloths, newspapers, aluminum cans, trash, debris, dead animals, or any other discarded, used or unconsumed substance which is not handled in accordance with the provisions of this article.     Multiple residential unit means any duplex, dwelling place or apartment, or group of apartments under a single roof, or in a single apartment complex, used for a dwelling place for more than a one-family unit and which is served by a single water meter.     Municipal solid waste means any solid waste derived from households, including garbage, trash and sanitary waste in septic tanks and includes solid waste for single-family and multifamily residences, hotels and motels, bunkhouses, campgrounds, picnic grounds, and day use recreation areas. The term includes yard trimmings and commercial solid waste, but does not include solid waste from mining, agricultural or silvacultural operations or industrial processes or operations.     Municipal solid waste disposal facility means any facility or location where the final deposition of any amount of municipal solid waste occurs, whether or not mixed or including commercial or industrial solid waste, including, but not limited to municipal solid waste landfills.     Municipal solid waste landfill means a disposal facility where any amount of municipal solid waste, whether or not mixed with or including commercial waste, industrial waste, nonhazardous sludges or small quantity generator hazardous waste, is disposed of by means of placing an approved cover thereon.     Owner means any person, firm, corporation owning, leasing, renting, occupying or managing any premises.     Plastic bag means a polyethylene or other heavy-duty plastic bag meeting the National Sanitation Foundation Standard of 1.1 mills and not exceeding a 30-gallon capacity, with securing twist tie. An untied plastic bag shall not be an approved container.     Retail tire dealer means a person actively engaged in the business of selling new and used replacement tires.     Rubbish means a variety of nonrecyclable household waste derived from places of residence and shall include paper, rags, plastics, cartons, boxes, broken glass bottles and jars, crockery, rubber, discarded clothing, and similar materials.     Scrap tire means a tire that is no longer suitable for its original intended purpose because of wear, damage or defect.     Scrap tire carrier means any person engaged in picking up or transporting scrap tires not otherwise exempted in the Georgia Rules for Solid Waste Management for the purpose of removal to a scrap tire processor, end user or disposal facility.     Scrap tire generator means any person who generates scrap tires. The term "scrap tire generator" may include, but is not limited to, retail tire dealers, retreaders, scrap tire processors, automobile dealers, private company vehicle maintenance shops, garages, service stations, and city, county and state governments.     Scrap tire processor means any person who is approved by the environmental protection division to receive scrap tires from scrap tire generators or scrap tire carriers for the purpose of scrap tire processing.     Scrap tire sorter means any person, other than the original scrap tire generator, who handles mixed tires by separating used tires and retreadable casings from scrap tires.     Single residential unit means any dwelling place occupied by one-family unit and which is served by a single water meter.     Solid waste means any garage or refuse; sludge from wastewater treatment plants; solid, liquid, semisolid, or contained gaseous material resulting from operations; mineral matter; metal and wooden furniture; appliances; large metal scraps and wires; wooden crates, boxes or pallets; dead animals; and other waste in a solid or semisolid state not otherwise defined in this section.     Waste means discarded material including, but not limited to, ashes, building refuse, garbage, hazardous waste, industrial refuse, recyclable waste, rubbish, solid waste, yard debris, tires, sand, gravel, slag, brick bats, trash, debris, dead animals, bottles, cans, boxes, containers, papers, tobacco products, appliances, mechanical equipment or parts, building or construction materials, tools, machinery, wood, motor vehicles or parts, vessels, aircraft equipment, waste oil, batteries, antifreeze, sludge from wastewater treatment plants or air pollution control facilities, and any other discarded material or substance of every kind and description resulting from domestic, industrial, commercial, governmental, or other operations.     Wheeled container means a covered plastic or rubber container on wheels designed primarily for use by residential units for storage of garbage, miscellaneous refuse, trash and other waste.     White goods means appliances such as stoves, refrigerators and other bulky household items primarily constructed of metal, parts of appliances, metal parts and miscellaneous metal.     Yard debris means tree limbs, branches, stumps and logs, twigs, grass and shrub trimmings and clippings, bushes, weeds, leaves, and general yard and garden waste materials, and includes stone and dirt rakings and similar waste materials resulting from landscaping activities.     Yard trimmings means leaves, brush, grass clippings, shrub and tree prunings, discarded Christmas trees, nursery and greenhouse vegetative residuals, and vegetative matter resulting from landscaping development and maintenance, other than mining, agricultural and silvacultural operations. (Ord. No. O-06-11-41, exh. A, § 13-110, 11-16-2006) 
Sec. 90-366. - Penalties for violation of article.     Except as otherwise specifically provided in this article, any violation of this article shall be subject to punishment in the municipal court of the city, upon conviction of such violation, as provided in section 1-8. (Code 1986, § 13-130) 
Sec. 90-367. - Litter. (a)  Scattering refuse and litter prohibited. No person shall throw or deposit any rubbish on any public or private street or scatter such refuse or litter on any public or private property, or throw or deposit in any stream or drainage area. (b)  Use of streets and roads. It shall be unlawful for any vehicle transporting loose materials to transport the same without a suitable cover securely fastened to the vehicle in such a manner as to prevent said loose material from being deposited on the streets and adjoining areas. (c)  Unlawful dumping. It shall be unlawful for a person to deposit, throw, drop, dump or otherwise leave any litter on the premises of another without the consent of such other person and without complying with the applicable laws including, but not limited to this section. (d)  Prima facie case. Whenever litter is thrown, deposited, dropped or dumped from any motor vehicle, boat, airplane, or other conveyance in violation of this section, the trier of fact may in its discretion and in consideration of the totality of the circumstances infer that the operator of the conveyance has violated this section. (e)  Presumption. Whenever any litter which is dumped, deposited, thrown, or left on public or private property in violation of this section is discovered to contain any articles, including, but not limited to, letters, bills, publications, or other writings which display the name of the person thereon in such manner as to indicate that the article belongs or belonged to such person, it shall be an rebuttable presumption that such person has violated this section. (f)  Emergencies. Nothing contained in this section shall require the intermediate measures where the violation is of such nature or degree as to constitute an immediate, clear, and present danger to the health and safety of the public. (Ord. No. O-06-11-41, exh. A, § 13-125, 11-16-2006) State Law reference— Litter control, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-40. 
Sec. 90-368. - Administration and enforcement of article. (a)  The city manager or his designee shall be responsible for the administration and enforcement of the provisions of this article. He may call upon the police department for assistance in its enforcement. All regulatory actions of the city manager or his designee shall be subject to review and approval of city council or a committee of city council designated for such purpose by the mayor. (b)  Upon determining that a violation of this article exists, the city manager or his designee shall cause written notice of such violation to be issued to the owner or occupier of the subject premises, setting forth the violation of the chapter and granting such owner or resident a reasonable time, not to exceed ten days, for the owner to correct said condition. (c)  Upon determining that the owner has failed or refused to correct the condition within the time prescribed in the notice, the city manager or his designee shall cause a notice to be issued directing the owner or occupier of said premises to appear in the municipal court to answer the charge of violation of this article. (Ord. No. O-06-11-41, exh. A, § 13-128, 11-16-2006; Ord. No. O-2015-15, 7-23-2015) 
Sec. 90-369. - Offal defined; removal to designated area; time limitation. (a)  The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:     Offal means the inedible parts of a butchered animal and waste parts of the animal. (b)  All offal and byproducts which result from the slaughter of an animal within the city shall be removed to the area designated by the county commissioners by the person responsible for slaughtering said animal within 12 hours after the slaughter of the animal. (Ord. No. O-06-11-41, exh. A, § 13-127, 11-16-2006) 
Secs. 90-370—90-396. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - COLLECTION 
Sec. 90-397. - Waste collection responsibility of city. (a)  The city shall be responsible for the collection and disposal of all garbage, solid waste, yard debris and rubbish within the city, and no person, unless otherwise authorized by a contract with the city, shall collect and dispose of or transport over the streets of the city any of such waste without first obtaining a written permit from the city to do so. Notwithstanding the foregoing, the city shall be authorized to enter into a contract with a private corporation or a public authority to provide for the collection and disposal of all garbage, solid waste, yard debris, and rubbish within the city. Such contract shall contain such terms and conditions as authorized by the city council and shall be for such length of time as may be determined by the city council and its citizens, but in no event shall such contract extend a length of time not otherwise authorized by the Constitution and laws of the state. (b)  The city shall not be responsible for the collection of hazardous waste and industrial refuse except as otherwise provided herein. The city shall not be responsible for the collection of building refuse generated by a contractor or other person who does not own or occupy the premises where such building refuse is generated. The city shall not be responsible for the collection of more than one cubic yard of residential building refuse generated in any one-week collection period by a person who owns or occupies the premises where such building refuse is generated. The disposal of all such waste, which is not subject to collection by the city, shall be the responsibility of the person generating such waste. Such waste shall be disposed of in accord with local, state and federal statutes, ordinances and regulations. One cubic yard shall be the equivalent of the size of two-wheeled garbage containers used for residential garbage collections. (c)  No person who owns or occupies any premises in the city shall permit trash, garbage, or other waste or rubbish to collect or remain on such premises, except during such periods between waste pickup; and no person who owns or occupies any premises in the city shall permit garbage, trash or other waste to be scattered from such premises into the public streets of the city. (d)  Any owner of property who permits garbage, solid waste, building refuse, yard debris, recyclable waste and rubbish, hazardous waste or industrial refuse to become in a condition which is hazardous or dangerous to the public health, safety and welfare shall be notified in writing by the city manager or his designee to abate such condition within ten days of the date of such notice. In the event that such condition is not abated within the time provided in such notice, then the city shall be authorized, either directly or through a private contractor, to abate such condition, and the cost of such abatement shall be charged against the property and shall be collected in the same manner as a lien for taxes is collected. (Ord. No. O-06-11-41, exh. A, § 13-111, 11-16-2006; Ord. No. O-09-08-27, 8-20-2009; Ord. No. O-2015-15, 7-23-2015) 
Sec. 90-398. - Refuse collection by city. (a)  The city, or any entity with which the city has contracted for such purposes, shall make collections of waste from residential premises which have wheeled containers at least once weekly. The particular day or days of each week during which such collection shall occur shall be determined by the city manager or his designee or agent. (b)  The city, or any entity with which the city has contracted for such purposes, shall make collections of waste from commercial and industrial premises which have wheeled containers at least weekly. The particular day or days of each week during which such collection shall occur shall be determined by the city manager or his designee or agent. (c)  The city, or any entity with which the city has contracted for such purposes, shall make collections of residential building refuse not exceeding one cubic yard in size on a schedule and at such times as may be determined by the city manager or his designee. One cubic yard shall be the equivalent of the size of two, wheeled garbage containers used for residential garbage collection. (d)  Yard debris and yard rubbish shall be collected by the city, or by any entity with which the city has contracted for such purposes, at least once a week on a schedule at such times as may be determined by the city manager or his designee or agent of the city. Such waste shall only be collected by the city when placed curbside. Wheeled containers shall not be utilized for disposal of such waste. (e)  Industrial refuse shall be collected from business and commercial premises a minimum of twice weekly and a maximum of five times weekly, based upon the need of the customer, according to such schedule as may be determined by the city manager or his designee or agent of the city. Such collection shall be made from a front-loading container. (f)  For purposes of this section, any resident of any multiple residential or commercial unit authorized to dispose of its waste by use of a front-loading container shall not be required to comply with the recyclable waste disposal provisions of this division. (Ord. No. O-06-11-41, exh. A, § 13-112, 11-16-2006; Ord. No. O-09-08-27, 8-20-2009; Ord. No. O-10-05-17, 5-20-2010; Ord. No. O-10-08-27, 8-19-2010; Ord. No. O-2015-15, 7-23-2015) 
Sec. 90-399. - Garbage containers. (a)  It shall be the duty of any owner or occupant of any single or multiple residential or commercial unit to place the wheeled container provided for such purpose on the assigned collection day at a front curbside location in such a manner as not to obstruct pedestrian passage, except that the city manager or his designee or agent may require the wheeled container to be placed on any side of a parcel of property for the reasons of topography or efficiency. (b)  It shall be the duty of the owner or occupant of a single or multiple residential or commercial unit to place the wheeled container at an appropriate curbside location at or before 7:00 a.m. or prior to the arrival of the sanitation truck. (c)  It shall be the duty of the owner or occupant of any single or multiple residential or commercial unit to remove the wheeled container from the curbside location to a storage location, which storage location shall be nearer to the unit located on the premises than to any street abutting such premises; provided, however, that said removal shall be accomplished not later than 7:00 p.m. on the day the contents thereof are collected. (d)  Garbage containers must be placed at least three feet away from vehicles, poles, fire hydrants, fences, overhead wires, low-hanging trees, branches, limbs, or other types of cover. (e)  It shall be unlawful for any person to set fire to the contents of, indiscriminately scatter or disperse the contents of, or otherwise vandalize any container provided by the municipality or its agent for the dumping of garbage. (Ord. No. O-06-11-41, exh. A, § 13-113, 11-16-2006; Ord. No. O-2015-15, 7-23-2015) 
Sec. 90-400. - Precollection practices. (a)  Front-loading containers. The city manager or his designee or agent shall determine the type, size, specifications, number and location of the garbage containers and shall determine the condition. (b)  Secure containers. All containers shall be maintained at all times with tight-fitting lids or covers, and secured in such a manner as to prevent the overturning by the elements or by dogs or other animals. (c)  Garbage. Garbage placed in containers for collection shall be enclosed in disposable watertight plastic bags with the top secured and placed in the container. (d)  Liquid. Garbage shall be drained of all liquids prior to its being placed in the container. (e)  Injurious garbage or trash items. Garbage placed for pickup with the potential for injury, such as broken glass, lightbulbs, sharp pieces of metal, fluorescent tubes, etc., shall be securely packaged or wrapped in such a manner to prevent injury to collection crews or other persons. (f)  Pet litter. Pet litter must be placed in securely tied plastic bags not to exceed ten pounds in weight and placed in the container. (g)  Clean container. It shall be the responsibility of the owner or lessee of the property to keep the container clean and free of odor. (h)  Scrap tires. No person shall deposit a scrap tire in any garbage container or on any public or private property. (i)  Dead animals. No dead animals shall be deposited in any garbage container. (j)  Burying or burning litter or waste; written consent. No owner or occupant of any such property within the corporate limits shall bury or burn litter or waste without prior authorization and written consent from the applicable regulatory agency, including, but not limited to, the United States Environmental Protection Division and/or the state forestry commission. Nothing in this provision shall authorize or be construed to permit the burial or burning of any material which is otherwise prohibited by state and/or federal law. (k)  Accumulation. No owner or occupant of any property shall cause, suffer, or allow the accumulation on his premises, of garbage, litter or waste where such material creates or causes a health hazard to neighbors or other citizens, or which is unsightly or emits foul or obnoxious odors. (l)  Violations. The conduct described in subsections (h), (j) and (k) of this section shall constitute a separate violation of this article for each day the garbage, litter or waste material remains or continues to unlawfully pollute, contaminate or burn on such premises. (Ord. No. O-06-11-41, exh. A, § 13-114, 11-16-2006; Ord. No. O-2015-15, 7-23-2015) 
Sec. 90-401. - Garbage collection for disabled persons.     Any person who is a full-time resident of a residential unit and who is disabled to the extent that such person is incapable of moving the wheeled container and who shall obtain a physician's certificate as to such disability, shall not be required to place the wheeled container at curbside as required in section 90-399. This section shall not apply unless all of the persons residing in a residential unit are disabled and obtain such physician's certificate. Provision for the collection of garbage from disabled residents shall be included in any contract approved by the city council under section 90-397. (Ord. No. O-06-11-41, exh. A, § 13-115, 11-16-2006) 
Sec. 90-402. - Sorting, storing, composting and collecting yard trimmings. (a)  Yard trimmings, and other small debris generated from the maintenance of a yard shall be collected and placed at the curb of the residence for collection. Said items are to be bagged or placed inside a container with a lid before being placed at the curb for pickup. (b)  The on-site composting of yard trimmings and other yard debris is encouraged. Further, the development of low-maintenance landscaping is encouraged for all commercial and industrial developments. (c)  Storing of yard trimmings and other debris generated on-site for a use other than in a composting or landscaping effort is hereby prohibited. (d)  Limbs and yard trimmings which cannot be bagged as required under subsection (a) hereof, shall be placed at the curb for pickup and shall be subject to the following limitations: (1)  Limbs and yard trimmings no more than five inches in diameter must be cut to no more than five feet long; (2)  Limbs and yard trimmings measuring from five inches to 12 inches in diameter must be cut to no more than one foot long. (3)  No limbs or yard trimmings larger than 12 inches in diameter shall be picked up by the city or by any entity with which the city has contracted. (e)  Yard trimmings and limbs shall be picked up on vacant lots, but only when such debris is generated from the vacant lot. (f)  Yard waste bags or containers must be placed at least six feet away from vehicles, trees, poles, fences, mailboxes, fire hydrants, low-hanging trees, limbs, branches, power lines, guy wires, or other types of obstructions. (g)  Lawn services and contractors are responsible for bagging the yard waste and other waste that they generate and disposing of it in a suitable location as identified by this division. (h)  Grass clippings, weeds, leaves, and other small yard waste materials must be bagged or placed in a container with a lid prior to being placed at the curb for pickup. (i)  Yard waste bags may be placed in the right-of-way, the street pavement or in roadside ditches as long as the flow of water or the flow of traffic is not inhibited or changed. (Ord. No. O-06-11-41, exh. A, § 13-116, 11-16-2006; Ord. No. O-09-08-27, 8-20-2009; Ord. No. O-10-05-17, 5-20-2010; Ord. No. O-10-08-27, 8-19-2010) 
Sec. 90-403. - Prohibitions. (a)  Yard trimmings. It shall be unlawful to place or mix yard trimmings with municipal solid waste within the city. (b)  Yard trimmings disposal . Yard trimmings shall not be disposed of at any municipal solid waste disposal facility having a liner and leachate collection system or requiring vertical expansion located within the city or the county. (c)  Stormwater collection system. It shall be unlawful for any person to dump any solid waste on any property, in any waters or in any stormwater collection system, except as authorized by applicable permits it shall be the burden of the alleged violator to show proof of any applicable permits. (d)  Storm drains. No person shall place any litter, refuse, trash, trees, grass, or other rubbish over or within five feet of a storm drain, drop inlet, culvert, or manhole. (e)  Appliances. No person shall leave outside in any building or in a place accessible to children any appliance, refrigerator, freezer, or other container which has an airtight snap lock or similar device without first removing therefrom the door. This section shall not apply to any appliance, refrigerator, or container which has been placed on or adjacent to the rear of the building and which has been crated, strapped, or locked so that it will be impossible for a child to obtain access to any compartment thereof. (f)  Dumping. It shall be unlawful to dump, open dump, or permit the dumping of litter, waste, scrap tires, municipal, commercial, or industrial solid waste or recyclables at any place within the corporate city limits including and without limitations, in or on any public highway, road, street, alley, or thoroughfare, including any portion of the right-of-way, any public or private property in the city or any waters in the city unless such litter or waste originates within the corporate limits of the city and the property is designated by the city council or its duly designated agent for the disposal of the above, and the material is placed into a receptacle or container designed for such property; and the property has a valid solid waste handling permit issued by the state environmental protection division (EPD) when required. (Ord. No. O-06-11-41, exh. A, § 13-117, 11-16-2006) 
Sec. 90-404. - Damaging, etc., containers; enforcement of regulations. (a)  No person shall overhaul, damage, or interfere with the contents of any wheeled container or adjacent containerized trash set out for collection for emptying or removal by the city, unless by permission of the city manager or his designee or agent. (b)  The city manager or his designee or agent is assigned the responsibility for enforcement of waste collection procedures enumerated herein. (Ord. No. O-06-11-41, exh. A, § 13-120, 11-16-2006; Ord. No. O-2015-15, 7-23-2015) 
Sec. 90-405. - Scrap tires. (a)  The owner or occupant of any premises shall be responsible for the sanitary handling and disposal of all scrap tires on the premises used or occupied by such person. (b)  It shall be unlawful to cause, suffer or allow the dumping of scrap tires at any place including, and without limitations, in or on any public highway, road, street, alley, or thoroughfare, including any portion of the right-of-way thereof, any public or private property or any waters unless the property is designated by the city council and the state environmental protection division for the collection or disposal of scrap tires and the person is authorized to use such property.
